O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Here is the translation:
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would accomplish this with the treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is estranged from everything, thus the science is lost and decayed, and nothing remains of the fires except for small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed off and the science is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I want to vivify the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will assemble the forms of the iron instruments of cautery, and of the other tools of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, it is the art of medicine extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it behooves him who undertakes to immerse himself in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of members, and the forms and conjunctions and separations of them, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and brains and the number of holes, and the movement and of moving veins and of resting ones, and where they issue from.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason said Hippocrates that the names with the name are not much, and with the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and likewise in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, if he does not take care, he will fall into error and harm people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Thus I have seen many of those who engage in this science, and then abandon it, lacking knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I see a foolish doctor who treats an abscess on the neck or throat of a woman, and treats the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another doctor who treated a stone of a man's kidney, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he took out with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called by the patient to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if one touched it, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another doctor who took in care Duke Henry of our land who had a broken leg, and with the breakage he had a wounded place;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the doctors, out of ignorance, held the breakage steady over the wound with very strong force, and did not leave the wound any calmness, and left it thus in torment;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded that it not be touched at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and then it happens that the leg becomes completely swollen and the feet and comes to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and release the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I had it reset it was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the way the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the limb was almost entirely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wound that burst open an abscess, and then it became inflamed due to the evil of its dominance.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is full of melancholic humor, it does not seem that one should touch it with iron unless it is in a place where one can completely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, dear sons, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	it is to know, namely where there is danger in many dispositions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For it is necessary that you beware, so that foolish mirrors cannot speak evil of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your arms in a crossing, and you undertake your wounded limbs lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to health and are praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let the grievous diseases be alleviated of painful sanity;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove your arms from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you may be able to come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says among some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take a bad disease in hand, lest you be called foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauterization and medicinal cautery, and these chapters are organized from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and about the forms of instruments, and the iron tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it is the chapters arranged in order and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is arranged according to the low head just as feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Here is the translation:
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid, and of harm, are the longest discourse and subtle science and hidden responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and about this spoke the wisest of the wise men, and agreed with this;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I suffered little for their words, because I reduced the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally to every complexion where there is matter, before the complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	it is to know cold temperament without material, and dry temperament without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a cold and dry complexione together with material, they devised none and said that cautery is great aid;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not suitable for a disease that comes from cold and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a cold disease with cold, nor through dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he said that those who say the opposite, that cautery makes great aid to cold and dry diseases that come in the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because you examine the body of the man and his moisture according to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true many times through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in no way should one interfere with those who have experienced it, and who know through long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the outcomes and the space of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other complexions we have no less fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the mirrors assembled and agreed with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that assembling fire is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than medical cauterization.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come except to the member that is cooked, and does not harm another member if it is not named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The burning remedies pass from one member to another by connecting, and bring to the affected limb grievous sanitation diseases;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and sometimes it kills the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire, due to its height and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experiment and through the length of service and study that I put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse myself from the length of the speech, because it does not please me that I remove the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out bodily diseases, as the philosopher said in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	For you receive in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agree on what time the cauterizations should be done, and they select the suitable moments.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the sudden injuries are often alleviated by the aid of cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and meanwhile the cauteries are for necessary pains and sudden injuries that cannot wait for the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think only of this, dear son, as foolish people customarily do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the illness that is healthy through cautery has no relapse;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so as they believe, because cauteries are not just medicine that changes the complexion, and dries up the humors that are cause of the pain, and is more valuable than medicine for the hastiness of its value, and for the virtue of its work and its signory.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it happens that the disease becomes worse at times according to the patient's temperament and the location of the disease and its severity.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and are gathered in him the excesses through the acquisition of food and similar things, so that it is not administered cauterization at the location where there is little excess and moisture, just as cauterization of denseness for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	but it happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization is worth anything after medicine, but their intentions are false, and it is cauterization the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of cures for any disease and they do not work, then we administer cauterization, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient ones said that cauterizers of golden instruments are more effective than those of iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of gold and because of the height of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the handles of cauterizers do not make putrefaction, but this is not true because I have tried it, and I have found that it is true in some homes;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and golden cauterizers are more valuable than those of iron, as they told us.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And however when you heat a golden instrument, you do not know when it is heated by the color of gold, and it is quickly cooled;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	they make to the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough of impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use cauterization of iron that we have made more suitable to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter according to the chief joints just below, because it is easier to find the way.
dou cautere olivaire	for fire cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are good for moisture and cold on the brain, and in it there is a remedy made by the cause of a disease called "soda", and by the cause of many humors which descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and for multitude of noises and pain of teeth and pain of throat, and also for all diseases that come from cold if like paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine modifying the chief three or four times, according to whether the strength and the age and the habituation of the patient can suffer it;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the patient rest the injured head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on your shoulder;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	afterwards put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and there where the two veins meet, if it bleeds from the gum, then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", because that is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And put it on the marked spot of ink, and do it by descending and extracting your hand little by little while twisting;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand suddenly, and turn the spot so you see the bone I little hole;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, then recommence the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	afterwards take a little silk, and put in warm and soft cotton inside, and put on the spot, and leave it three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after putting a millstone on the buttocks;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it be until the swelling is reduced;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing the wound of the joint which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the old men said that when the wound stays open for a longer time, it purges more;
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore it helps to move.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one should not leave the cautery so long that part of the bone is burned, and then reset what is burned of the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should cauterize so much to leave it thus, and strike strongly so that the bone is exposed as widely as the circle that women put on their thighs, because the humors issue forth.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards one should cure and sew it up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some cases where there is a risk of fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should let them grow;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by the continuous natural solutions, as we demonstrate in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and similarly when the head of a patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more salubrious and mild for me, and I usually work in assembling a healthy condition.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When the entire head is afflicted with chronic pain, and it lasts a long time, then one should use the remedies of iris and pills that are called "cochie", and purging of the head and eyes and applying plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery that we mentioned before, it is not worth it.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the head of the patient is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize beneath this one a little bit, as we said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After making fire cautery on some curved horn of the head just to the bone, as we said before, and make the cautery where it is called "vasselez".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the joints in which one puts ventouses;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and hold your hand so that you do not touch just to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patients feel too much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the moisture of the head, and this is the method:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head sudden pain comes, and the disease has spread to the eye, and the head is purged by mundane medicines, and other treatments that I have said in the division of diseases are made, and all this does not profit at all:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then you make cauteries according to two manners, that is to know of medicine by water and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauteries of medicine by water are that you prick a sweet deal of salt, and remove the crust and recover the poultice as the head, and then make the temple where the pain holds in such a way that you can restore the deal of salt beneath the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it will be restored, bind it and hold it well and let it thus for 12 hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then unbind it and pull out the deal of garlic, and leave the wound thus for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on a cotton cloth soaked in butter until it makes a scab.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of the wound, until it is healthy;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that I have written or described twelve treatments of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery to the form that it is in:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the form of a nail or it has little curvature, and in a small appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and twist the iron a little more lightly, so that most of the thickness of the cauterizing fire is absorbed;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the artery does not become hardened, which is furthest, and runs with abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards put cotton on the wound, and place it on the spot for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I put moist cotton in a poultice, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healthy;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this emigrated wound with the cautery called "cultellare", at every point, and beware of cutting the artery in this emigrated wound which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the migration
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not profit, and you see that the cauteries mentioned beforehand in medicine do not soothe it, then it is necessary to heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it becomes white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and signify thus on the dull eye a line of half a finger's length, and lift your hand once, and hold steady so you do not touch the artery and do not approach up to the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and guard against the mandible that moves when one chews, and the nerves have no regard except for the movement and that spasm does not come to the patient, and guard against the disorder of blood in the artery when it will be touched, or touching has great fear and mistrust to him who does not know it, and who is not a student and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the vein grow in my way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it flows.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the enemy at the head as we have said, and heal the wound until it is healthy;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or chapter of extracting the artery, with the cautery that has two cuticles;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and these are better cauteries than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from cold, and one has tried medicines that dissolve and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then heat this cautery which is called "points", because it is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After puncturing all around the ailing ear, or around the two where the pain holds in both, and slightly dislodge it beneath the root of the ear before you have signed the place of the incision;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and let him have points touched behind each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing, let the limb be sound.
de la torture de la bouche	from the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Pain that must be healed by fire cautery is not fiercer than those that move with inflammation, as we have said in the divisions of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make a cautery on similar things that come from dryness and spasms of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this type of pain that moves with inflammation and evacuations of the head and gagging, and it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and another a little above the temple, and the third at the joint of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and have it cauterized at the top of the ear a little below the crown of the head, and another in the temple as long as a thumb;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery iron stay on as long as it takes for the worst of the heat to subside;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the cutting instrument that we have mentioned before, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the cuts be a bit larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing the limb as I said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When the apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then you perform four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the head, and one on the limb called "vassels" as we have said before, and the fourth cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large pills and Mondifian powders to calm the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	afterwards take the entire head of the patient and place on the occiput a plaster of Sinapis, which is written or treated in the treatises of plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of cauterization:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is thus healthy, it is good.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, make three cauterizations on the skin of the head descending to the neck, and let there be a space between each cauterization of two fingers' width.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it as the others, and if you see it is necessary, and the patient is suffering, make one cauterization in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the mastery is, two others on the two horns, and treat until he is healthy.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauterers who are called "olivares" as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of years and of that which we have said before.
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	afterward cleanse the head of the patient, then make a cauterization on the head and on each horn, and behind and thirdly on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you have more mastery, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is strong, then make four cauterizations on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let it be until the worst of the heart is burned, and lift your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the treatment until he is healthy, and let the cauterers who are called "olivares" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to purify the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is severely suffering and unable to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear the suffering, then make him gargle and chew mundifying food often with good meat.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after the king's head is in a mirror, and you make fire cautery according to what we said before, and you apply the cautery to the little vessel, and to each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and resilient, you make fire cauteries as I said to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the olive-tree cautery be according to the manner that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, make them undergo subtle fire cauterization according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause of melancholy is excessive or corrupt and gross moisture, then cauterize with such fire cauterizations as we said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause of melancholy is excessive declining into melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will clear their brain, according to what was said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king's head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after you make a well-made trephine, also like a circle, if you put it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient is crossed, and may be well held from all parts;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after presenting the limb, and it is moved by the burst of old herbs;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and the heat is tempered with fire, so that the fingers can be applied to suffer the pus;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after viewing the circle inward within the head, and let it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient every week once with another good government, until he is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Where you want to cauterize, make points more often all along the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cauterization moisturizes the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on a cotton wool moistened in butter and in grease of goose.
de l’awe des eulz	of the warmth of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When warmth comes first to the eyes through the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give drink to the patient thing humecting the head, and ward off all moisture, and make sweat or bathe many times a day.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After he commands his head to be cooled, and have him cauterized within the head, and have two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the water is with both eyes together, or in one if the descent is in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and touch all the cauteries to all the veins and arteries that are beneath the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, then stain it with a little powder as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you about extracting arteries and incising the cautery, how you will apply it.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes one performs cautery or hastening beneath the two hindmost bones.
dou cors des larmes	at the course of the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are ancient and accustomed and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the deformed head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is from the cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then I make the cautery that I mentioned at the beginning of the treatise, descending to the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I perform cautery in the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or hastening beneath the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it is more affected, then one should cauterize gently above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	at the course of the tears through the depths of the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you administer medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit him, then give three cups of broth to the sick person.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king's head, and make a cautery or a thousand gold cauteries;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries of the cautery that is called "clavulis" on the two ulcers, a little below the eyebrows;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery that you do not puncture it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the papier (pupil) of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	of that which is in the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that make two cauteries on the two ulcers as long as the eyelashes are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave your hand there unless the third part of the skin is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	It sometimes happens that the hair of the eyes is converted into a pustule, and pricks the eye, and one makes cauteries according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	it's to know about fire, or ardent medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in good health;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after marking on the paper of the eyes a figure that is as similar as the dead leaf, and let it be the beginning of the sign from the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put moist cotton in a gleam of egg and musk of pearl on the eye, then heat the cautery to the form that is there;
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked little by little many times, so that the heat should be there at that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retract, and the hairs rise to the tip of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then I put moist cotton in a blistering way until the inflammation is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of the joint so that it becomes healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after that the hairs grow, and the skin is softened then recommence the cautery on the same spot, just as you did previously;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are burned, then cauterize until the skin is lifted to its natural place, and is even, and does not prick the eye with hairs.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The medical cauterizers are that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even, then make a parchment in the shape of the leaf of myrtle.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and lively chalk, of each one a Z., and crush well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it quickly, so that it does not cool down, then sprinkle on the form that you have made like the leaf of a mirror, and put on the paper of eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease holds in one only solvent, then should one open in one, and if both are alike thus;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put beneath the oil cotton wadding in a egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and let the head of the patient be in your health and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press the poultice and the wadding all the times that the patient feels biting of the medicine, for it feels biting as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have made them grow long, then apply medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the biting is past, lift the skin of the wound, and reward yourself if you see the paper lifted as if it had been lifted by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if he is thus, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If this does not work, then put more medicine on the wound or the medicine has not worked, so that your operations are equal, and your eyes are in focus;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a soft cloth moistened in a warm potion so that the bitter hearts are clear, after curing the wound of the joint which is called "dyafenis" and others, so that it may be healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to take good care of your work with great attention so that there is no lack in the medicine as eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the parchment becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then recommence the medicine on that wound which is softened by the proper parchment, just as you have done before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the cure so that it may be healthy.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the leaf of dead myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and adjust your constrictions accordingly.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let him not stray from the straight path to whom it is the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you perform cautery according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in a healthy position;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor does it nod.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then apply a moist cotton cloth to the affected eye or to the juice of persillation upon the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	then heat the cautery which is thus prepared:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaped to the head like the form of a hollow pen, so that it may be the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, it should be pointed from one part of the head to the other, and if you see, it should also be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but always, this which is shaped thus is suitable for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing on the fistula, it is uncovered, and one draws out the pus, and the dryness.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and it is closed, if it opens, and one draws out the fluid from the bowl;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after placing the hot iron on the cautery site, and holding your hand on the cautery at the part of the nail next to the eye, so that your hand does not make a fool;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If that does not work, then recommence the cautery once again, and another time you have mastery of it, and leave it three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after I place on a cotton pad in a poultice, and cure the disiccation of the ointment as long as it is healthy, and if 40 days pass without it being healthy, then I place on a medicine with corrosive acid so that the bone is uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the king according to what he would come into his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Then make a fistula, and close the wound.
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after putting it in the incision, I examine subtly what its shape is.
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make a quantity of an ounce of powder.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand firmly, and the patient does not move at all, so that the melted powder does not run to its eye.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye a cotton cloth moistened with egg whites or in water.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the powder if it reaches the wound of the fistula, and the healthy part by marvelous sanitation.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healthy through the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then one must administer powder to the nail, and bring the fistula back to its own proper place according to what is suitable for it.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks on the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks on the lips occur that are called "poils", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks of the bone that we have discussed in divisions, and the treatment does not benefit, then apply a small cautery scalpel according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And put it hastily in those cracks until it comes just to the font.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing the wound of the scab, until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the joint, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after having made putrid matter and rot and is inflamed and becomes a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit at all:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you apply the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron instrument comes to the front of it, and where behind it stays;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do thus once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it be healthy;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is cured thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and cut out the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	two movements of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicine but it does not help, then put the patient's head in a healthy position;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after heating the cautery whose form will come thus afterwards in such a way that you put a cane against the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and place the hot cautery hastily, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lifting your hand and reapplying the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	then fill the patient's mouth with salty water, and hold it for an hour and rinse forcefully.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the teeth that were moving are confirmed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupt moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or decay, and medical treatments are of no value, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cauterization of blister and cauterization of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cauterization of blister is such that you take blister of a cow, and the end in a spoon of iron or copper;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	after taking cotton and wrapping it around the point of a tent, and moistening it in blister water, and placing it on the aching tooth quickly and holding it until it cools;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that the moist cotton and blister water are cold, and place it on the aching tooth, and place in the hot iron so that the fire reaches the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cauteries together with fire are such that you take a cane of iron or copper, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After burning with fire cautery, because of this the wound will form crust afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled down.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be alleviated that same day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good warm water in the impression of that cautery, and then he should spit it out forcefully.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the form of a good cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a good cautery on the part of the body that you want, and according to what you are able to do.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and that is the form of the burn:
des scrophules	of the scalps
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are of humid and cold moisture, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then burn with fire cautery, because afterwards it will form crust, and have two openings for the fumes to exit from the cautery on the other part.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and put the cautery iron on the abscess once, or where it is, until it reaches the root of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, then put the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put on a cotton molehill in a poultice so that the discharge is drained away;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing, anoint the limb with ointments and tents until it be sound.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the humors collect on the channels of the arm, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be emptied first by soluble medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	after you do cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful that you do not come too close to the throat, and do not harden the skin but only a little;
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After the fire cautery, apply another cautery to the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle" because we have the shape in front;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal the limb as we have said before, so that it may be healthy.
de la toust	of the tonsils
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all the diseases of the lung are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever nor cough, and it is a chronic disease, then apply two cauteries to the ribs in their corners;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery between the nipples amidst the breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle" according to the shape mentioned before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see it, apply cautery by pricking to the entire cautery that is called "points" because the shape is thus before in the disease of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the skin be just to XXX, where they are inserted.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After curing the limb according to what has been said before, and let the cauteries be at three places according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because they are lighter cauteries, because you make three of them at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Then let the patient be rubbed on his back and on his sides;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift the heart that is within the swollen area with the fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, heat the cautery that has two points where it is in the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart as much as it pierces just to the side, and there would come the figure of the cautery along with three cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and because of this, cautery is done with the cautery that has three points, for which the figures of cauterization are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and they are the veins according to the subtlety of a thread and it is the form of the cautery that has three points;
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And at no time is it joined to this .i. nerve because it has .viij. cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After applying fire cautery, they burn with a hot iron;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after making the patient rest, and not moving their limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, little things happen there, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery claw, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is restored, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach coldness and much moisture gather there until they distort his complexion, and multiply the catarrh to him, and are accustomed manners of cures that do not profit, then it is necessary that the patient be supported on his back, and stretches out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	From that point on, I make three fire cauteries in the shape of a knife for the quantity of a finger, with each entire fire cautery, and two fire cauteries on the sides, so that the figure of the fire cauteries is at three angles, and has some space between one and another so they are not joined together when they are applied to the skin.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the fire cautery be so profound that it penetrates the two parts of the heart, and let the figure of the fire cauteries be according to this form without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a large fire cautery in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who will have fear of this fire cautery, will burn in pricking and sign on the stomach at that point according to the quantity that you see of an inch.
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Then cauterize all of the cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we had before, until it be healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver suffers from cold and moisture and great windiness, so much that it is far removed from its natural complexion through the superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit them at all, if it is necessary that the patient be anointed on their thigh;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and apply three cauteries according to this form and this shape and this quantity on the liver, below the hypochondries, where the humor or the seat of the pain comes;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and let there be a space between each cauterization the width of a finger;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cautery be two fingers' length from the body, and do not press too much with your hand on the entire cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	And let it be scorched so much that the worst of the heart is sweet, and let the patient's right hand be on their feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, let him lean back, and stretch out his legs, and lift his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and that is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if your wound is, if you cauterize these cauteries of the cutellarium, be subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the heart, for you would dry out the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it not come near the bouillon, for the heart is very subtle there, and you should beware to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too extreme;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if he is on the couch, he feels a wild pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment touches the mirrors, it is necessary that the patient be warned about his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then point out the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a reason, from which it takes its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery as much as the vein is burnt, and approach just to the siphac, until the porreture is entirely purified;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment, according to the treatment of the wounds, until he is healthy;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not suitable that anyone uses this cautery unless he who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and whose hands these diseases have corrected many times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can hardly work, and always it seems to me that it is better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of fire cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one must make multiple cauteries at the roots of aristologe, and in such manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristology as long as you can find it, the largest possible, and let it be dry, and also let it be as thick and as long as your fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and grind it into oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the shoulder and the neck, and apply small cauterizations a little downwards in the part that is beneath the beard;
