et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and apply cauterizations between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining backwards a little;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and apply cauterization in the thigh, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on both sides of the thigh opposite the cauterization that is between the shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press with your hand, but rather open it widely as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some old man said that no one uses fire cauterization similarly to the razor, and they heat it up and place it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and it hurts because we have said in the aposteme of the foolishness.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear where the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the worst
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the worst of what we have said as divisions of cures, and it does not benefit at all, then they add three kinds of cautery that are good for everything.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	In this manner it is necessary to make three or four incisions, in a line according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the cautery of the foolishness that we have said before.
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient be aware of it on his back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the heart which is next to the mouse, or where the stitches of the patient come from the left side, and let the elevations that you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After they boil the inflamed nerves until the pain is perceived on the other side, and then they apply the fire cautery, and thus they will have four.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see that the entire fire cautery is applied to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has obtained purification by long tension, and this is more than the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Fire cautery is not suitable for hydropsy, except in the manner that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat according to the methods that we have stated in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four fire cauteries around the bowel, and one below the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one on the thigh.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and let the fire cauteries be very close to the width of a finger.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After that, leave the fire cautery open for a long time to purify, and do not discontinue the treatment of the patient after the cautery.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will be assembled with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The form of the cautery for the belly should be the key that we have previously demonstrated.
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical, and are full of citrine water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and the anular.
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and raise your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not insert it too deeply, lest you would push back the yellow watery fluid, and let the cauterizing iron be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	Afterwards, apply two cauteries on each leg at the point of the cutellaire.
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauteries be of a length, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg.
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauteries on for a long time without removing them, so that the water goes out.
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the treatment of other treatments that we have said.
de la menoison	of the menorhea
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a stomach problem comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by methods of treatments;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong virtue, if you do the great cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before or cautery of the stomach, with circular cautery;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and 4 cauteries within the subtle bowel to all, and 1 cautery subtly on the clavicle, and 2 cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make them undergo cautery on the fingers, and apply cautery to each spot, and small cauteries on the stomach below the waist, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are in the foundation, or one or several, and are ancient and are of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit, if you do cauteries:
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	Here is the translation:
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	and if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the food does not digest, and one sees the face inflating, then he puts a great cautery on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the clavicle cautery.
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and let the cautery be applied for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing, let the limb be sound.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness that is named "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you touch the bruise, heat up the cautery that seems to be the remedy, and then apply it all burned on the touched bruise.
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and let your hand stay there until the cautery reaches the origin of the vein, so that the blood flows freely.
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do it once or twice, and if there is much bruising, cauterize each one as we have said.
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the treatment of swollen eyes, profitable as long as they are healthy.
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the affected area, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure the pain of a high temperature, which we will describe in its place, then comes such an illness that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes, and it is wrapped and casts putrid and corrupted moisture, if you want to prove all of a subtle tent, and beware that you know all of the tent how deep it has.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heating the cautery that seems to be a remedy, and put it in the fistula according to the quantity that the tenderness has entered, and recommence the cautery as long as the corrupt and rotten flesh is burned, one time, or two, or three, according to the quantity of their need.
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and guard against irritating the nerves that are affected, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestine, so guard against these evils, and do not make those false passages in the flesh, and think that it is not a permanent wound.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	after healing the flesh until it is healthy, and if the wound is sealed, and the materials are removed long afterwards, then know that the wound is entirely healthy.
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	and if the materials are not removed, it means the joints are twisted, and the bones at the font are corrupted;
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	and thus like one of those that we will direct to its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from fracture comes with cracks, and great windiness, and does not take heed of a woman, then it is necessary that you perform cauterization on the cracks on one side and on the other to the clavicle, which we have mentioned before.
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	and if we place the cauterizations in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and fragile from fracture and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then it is necessary to perform cauterization on the lower part above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin, and one on the right side and one on the left side, and each cautery should be as long as the width of a thumb.
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and you make a fire cautery on the back, where it is swollen above.
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	and let the cauteries be shaped according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow conception for that reason, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, it feels great pain:
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	then it is necessary to make three cauteries around the belly, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and make the cautery on the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cauteries be shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the viscous moisture descends to the box of the thigh, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and it is found that the looseness of the department is visible, so it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the box of the hip to a cautery similar to a circle, and mark in front of the joint within the box as it turns, so that the box is inside the circle.
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and if the cauteries are such as those with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if these cauteries are not present to you, make three cauteries of large olives, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the wounds.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until he is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the ankle
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes to the box of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated for what we have said in the division and the treatment is not effective, and the disease is ancient:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	Then it is necessary to purge the patient of thick, foul humors with filthy pills or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	After doing cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of doing cautery is according to two methods:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	it is to know simultaneously burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is according to many methods, of which one is such:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the surface of the thigh three triangular cauteries in this form, and make a good depth and large, and have between each cauterization the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped;
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	sometimes one makes a cauterization in the middle on top of the thigh, because there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, one should cauterize with a circular cauterization that we mentioned before in the case of dislocation of the thigh;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire thigh, and all the spaces of the skin are soothed by heat.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And it is the manner in which one does on the thigh, when the pain holds in the thigh, and does not reach as far as the knee nor as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, have them apply two cauteries there where the patient says the pain holds, and three fingers above the ankle on the left side a little.
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	and let the cautery be gentle, and let the heat of the skin be soothing.
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers from the foot or near the ankle, then cauterize where they feel the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if it is necessary, have them do more.
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	and if it is known that the pain is beneath the knee towards the thigh, have them apply a cautery with a gentle or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery so much that you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more great nuisance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have performed fire cautery on the shin of the foot, and they let it be so long that the leg became entirely swollen, and the feet also, and were pierced and corrupted all over the feet.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a flux of stomach from which he got death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, perform fire cautery on one and on the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise men teach about cautery of the thigh, that it is in this manner, make a iron like this and let it be at the top as big as a turnip seed, or a little less, and let it be between the skin and the muscle, and some of them are from one skin fold to another, measuring the quantity of a thumb's width.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the skin folds be above two fingers, and let them also be like knots, and have a well-made iron handle.
et c’est li forme:	and that is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And let it be heated until it is completely red hot and gives off sparks, and then put it on the affected thigh, and turn it towards the healthy side.
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and cauterize once with the cautery iron and let it be for three days.
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time.
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of joint as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its consequences, and we see few who make use of it.
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and however these are good cauteries, which can suffer, and there where they are beneficial.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The burning cauteries of medicine are such that you make the instrument at the crossing points where it descends to the edge of the door, and be it of iron or fire at a long perch, and in its height it has II among us, and each one has the quantity of the thickness of a finger.
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and be they open downwards and upwards, and join together in this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After putting on the box of the hip to the ailing person lying on his good side, and then you put your hand all on the box of the hip.
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After the hand is placed between the two circles of warm water which has been heated by fire, and let it stay there for an hour in the tension, and then the patient suffers from the heat and aridity.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For he finds numbness as if from fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the numbness has passed, he raises his hand with the instrument and lifts the warmth of sweet water, and lets it stay thus for three days, and puts on a poultice so that what is black from the burn should be ostended;
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and let it stay three days to purify in a strait;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and that would be the last aid after the treatment of wounds so that they are healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make him an instrument that holds warmth according to what you did for the wound earlier.
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and it is the manner of warm water, and I have written it in a treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take equal parts of alkaline and living chalk, as much of one as the other, and crush them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where there is a small opening somewhere so that the tip of a razor can enter;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put above that pot another well-plumbed pot, and put on alkaline and chalk and sweet warm water, until there is two fingers' depth of the powders that you will have well ground in your hand;
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and let it stand thus until the water descends and becomes warm and clear, or the well-plumbed pot, then take all that water, and pour it on chalk and alkaline as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very warm and is administered in many works of medicine and in cauteries of other members.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it makes other works like fires, and if there are other medicines where one cauterizes well the hinge thus as thesis and honey and nut oil and chalk with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure where one man was cured of the pain in his ankle and sciatic vein, and he had suffered greatly, and said that there was no other cure, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he was bathed as it is instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And you do in this manner that you take fresh and dry litargire, and crush it well with a little fat, and apply it to the ankle and thigh and leg where the pain is, and the binding.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and leave it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the bitterness.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter a warm bath so that his body is slightly relaxed, and make him enter his bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healthy.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery for such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with fiery cautery, it helps much;
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and it should be done, the cauteries in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and the warmth of old oil, and place it on the fossa that is between the thumb of the foot and the other called the instep.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After taking dry fiery sparks, and heating them at the fire until they become charcoal, and putting them on the wool, and leaving them until they are extinguished;
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and do it again thus, and do not cease from doing thus until you think by your sense that it comes just to the ankle, and that the pain has ceased;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of the shin".
de la dolor dou dos	from the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from a fall or percussion or by excessive evacuation, or by expansion of cold matter, none of these appearances is worth cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary after that the patient is emptied of filthy pills or other similar things, that one makes on their back, there where the pain holds, three marked lines of an inch, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can suffer.
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery that is called "points".
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see, make three or four cauteries on the cautious claw-shaped cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a constricted arm when they lift it, and fear.
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you find in the posterior spine of the back and in the appearance that comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, if you cauterize with the cautery of that according to this method.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery penetrates any part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that the cautery is applied around the spine with a piercing fire cautery on two or three lines, and the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the limb so that it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery in a curved area which is in a spasm of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	from the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When pain of joints is caused by moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which the doctor calls "podagre" properly, and when it is from cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in such manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make the mound of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a need to prick on the surface of the foot, you should make a complete cautery at every point that one calls a "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, then make a cautery on each knee, three cauteries or four of each part, with all olive-shaped cauteries.
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	and if you have a greater mastery, then make more, but do not hold your hand firm for longer than it takes for the warmth of the cauter to penetrate.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the fingers, two lines;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there remains a point of pain in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come just as cuts or just as swellings, cauterize each part, and make good government for the patient and prepare medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good government for him and you purge bad blood, he will be healthy with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	about the treatment of swelling
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture comes in the groin, and the bubbles descend to the loins and it is new, then you must cure the view when you look at it, so that it does not harm anyone on that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and he uses things that loosen the belly, if his farts come down from his belly;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his arm as long as the bubble is repaired, and put them in your hands, and mark from below the rupture on the bone of the thumb, and at all a sign that is similar to half a circle above the body;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then burn with fire cautery of the form that it is.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until he is pale and feels sensations.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bulbs to their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the ministers hold their hand on it so that they do not turn back;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and work well the thighs of the patient, and put the cushion under him and the sergeant on the thighs, and another under the foot that holds his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cautery on the sign at all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then recommence again another time until you come up to the bone;
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and watch subtly that the bubble does not burst when you do the cautery;
que tu ne le brulasses;	so that you do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and so that the patient does not die, or another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your operations are worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauteries of children be subtle according to the measure of their years, and of great people also great according to their measure.
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days, heal the wound with a cautery of borax so that the ecchymosis may be removed;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after healing other wounds so that it may be healthy, and lay the patient forty days on their back so that the wound may be well suppurated;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his bandages be loosened for a long time, so that the boils do not burst when he gets up to go to the chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, a well-made poultice is applied to him, and it is left on for forty other days.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and he should have good rest, so that he may exert himself little and beware of too great repletion of drinking and eating, and of too high pride.
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he makes this instruction, he will be entirely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will describe hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When wounds come to other areas and are chronic, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then make the fire cautery of the same quantity, and be careful with the third degree of burning.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the treatment according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that one should be cauterized with the fire at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the level of the notch and make a line according to the width above the root, and another below, and hold your hand in all the fire of the cauterizing instrument.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more moderate.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from ancient pain in any member (or limb)
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to a member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the treatment of medicine is of no value, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cauteries be according to the length of the member and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of torsions and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if he is healthy from the first cautery, it is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	by this name, recommend another cautery on that one, for such is the custom that it must be changed in the limb that is nearest to it, because it is necessary that you make the cauteries until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	of sickness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The messengers are often helped by cautery with great aid, and especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	You cannot see that it is cauterized, take care that the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend nor stay, and you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the chief.
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I place my head at the nave, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the veins;
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and it (the cautery) is on the two horns, and behind towards the hollow of the armpit;
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and I leave it (the hand) so that the cautery comes just to the bone, and until the scabs fall off if the vapors of the gross humors can issue forth;
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize on the worse according to what is before it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the mixture is scattered throughout;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it appears manifestly, if it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries that we have said above, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one on the chest and another on the flank, and two on the shoulders;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and it is on the joints, and it is on the Dou Pis tendons, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands;
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and beware of the nerves that are on the last ridge of the spine, so you do not burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that the more you do cautery, the more it does harm, and it doesn't profit;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and know that the patients do not feel any pain from the cautery if they are healthy and sense it, because the body is already totally corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manners of the iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing the wound with flour paste mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes in any member and is cured by medicines and oils and emplasters, and it is not completely healthy, then you should make cauteries on the member according to the size and smallness of the member;
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cauteries be a little deep within the breadth of the skin;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wounds so that they are healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And often one makes a cautery at the hand and at the foot and at the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus if it is stopped, the swelling disappears;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and never intervene unless one is knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of abscesses
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the engines of medicine are worthless, then cauterize with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the breadth of the skin, so that the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then heal with flour of fenugreek and of lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of the colon and blood of the almond tree, each a part.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be wholly together, and let it be tied with a bandage, and let it be elevated to the position until it is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of cancer by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a cancer appears at its onset, and you want to stop it, if you cauterize with the cautery that forms a circle, entirely around the tumor.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And meanwhile the wise men say that one should also perform cautery at the milky white spot of the cancer;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and meanwhile this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted to avoid it happening;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and more rightfully, it is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflammation that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When some have a disease that is called "adubelati", and it delays from being cured or due to the superfluousness that it does or due to the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and has little blood, or due to the tension;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you hasten to amputate:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then you cauterize around a lot of small cauterizations by pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	after that, let it be so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she hastens to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you perceive the entire fire cautery, heat the cautery to the form it is.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" so that the cauteries penetrate to the heart, and be such the cauteries that the patient feels them deeply in some manner that the course of the purification is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with fire through iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a mangling of a limb, for it eats away the members just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this disease in the patient who can suffer cauterization together with fire, then heat the small and large clavicle cauterizations very much, according to what is suitable for the patient or where the disease is;
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	after you cauterize all parts as much as you can reach all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted may be destroyed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and apply to the limbs cauteries suffering from burning with oil until the burns of hot fire are eliminated, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of swollen eyes producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it's good;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, then recommence the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted limbs.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this mangy condition is often cured by medical treatment with fire cauterization in the patient's limb;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but every way fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the treatment of the medicine for the disease in the division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take the amount you have in hand.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the pores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that our feet are affected by a disease called "clothes" according to our intention, and it is a big faulty thing which affects the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries of this disease are in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is that you heat it, I heated cautery as if it were a pen of vaulted wood, and make it from good iron to the measure that it can pierce the nail on all sides, and that it has subtle margins;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	afterwards, put it all hot upon the nail, and turn your hand totally around the nail until it reaches to the bottom of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and let it stay thus for three days until it begins to discharge pus;
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make a plaster of wild, savage, bruised mallows with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be disrooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the limb of inflammation by cleaning it so much that it becomes healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are turned away by bad ulcers on the body, and often occur on hands and feet, it is necessary that you apply warm water cautery.
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in such a manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a iron rod or a hollow tube, and place it on the nail and the joint, that is to know if there are varicose veins;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and place the rod on it so that it penetrates all around, then I put a little warm water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the rod reaches to the root of the nail, and thus finds the warm water way down to the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient suffer a little the biting of the warm water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave it thus, and it will remove everything to its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Here is the translation:
li cure dou trembler	the cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some shiver with cold or nerve weakness, or from quartan fever or another, if it is necessary that you apply three or four fire cauterizes on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach for an olive-shaped cautery;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	if you leave the shivering, and hasten the santifying of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of painful pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never appear by default through the body's baths, or pus-filled pustules, that come from gross corrupt materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	if it is necessary at first when they appear that one should apply fire cautery on each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle fire cautery of myrtle wood, so that the pointed end is heated by the fire, or from the root of a long aristology, or with a lentiform cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow worse from then on, but are freed from the superfluities that come with them, and are healthy.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great flowings of blood from the artery that is cut into the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cauterization of the limb, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And always when it happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold very tightly so that the blood is appeased beneath your finger, and does not issue forth anymore;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then apply to the fire the olive oil cauterizers, more small and large as they may be, until they are all red.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take I, or large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is located, and apply the cauterizer to that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cauterizer there until the blood is stanched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it happens to burst forth when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease from doing one after another until the wound is completely cleansed.
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and beware that you do not irritate the nerve that is weakened, and that another evil does not come onto the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and know that when the wound does not close over the artery, one cannot well restore it in the meantime while the artery is large, if it is not by one of the three methods that we have said:
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with a thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to restore blood;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and be tied and held firmly in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers the stanching of the blood in a narrow place, either by wrapping tightly with cloths or by putting things firmly on, or similar things, does not profit unless it is done promptly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if it happens to no one and there is no better medicine present, then one must put their finger index on the wound of the vein as we have said, and tightly bind until it is restored above the wound and above the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move the finger, but the mill of cold water often so that it be very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and rested;
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make an inquiry beforehand about those things which he has need of cauterizations and of medications.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book on surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have said in the first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or with burning medications, and the instruments and causes and materials and forms of cauterizations;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have placed that chapter of the loin just below the feet, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same method by which one finds more easily what one wants to cure.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus I begin it, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one on cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you that you do not undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	if they come from such who are wounded by their illness so that they die easily because of the weakness that they find in their disease, and the greatness of their evil.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and of these things one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And of these there is one who gives his judgment, and says:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am healed";
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the disease is despised.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but rather put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open foolishly but wisely of those things of which you are certain, and of which you can take and lose.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your diseases so that health may be converted.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you to acquire good renown, glory, and long memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and direction, and may you be willing to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Here is the translation:
dou chief plein d’aigue	a full head of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	You know that this illness comes very often to children at birth, and when the womb holds the child's head too tightly;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes it happens because of a response given by one who does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I never saw this illness except in children, and nearly all those that I have seen hastened death;
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in certain treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw the child whose head was full of water, and the head grew so much each day that it could not be sustained;
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture was so great that it became mortal, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone under the forehead, between the heart and the bone;
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the operations are such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make a large incision in the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and let it be as long as two of us, so that the moisture flows;
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see there the form of a spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make four incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see are the commissures of the head overturned on each part, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not respond to you:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	if it is necessary that you make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after cutting, remove all moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After holding the incisions with drapings and powders, and I put in wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day;
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then dislocate it, and treat the wound with tents and with ointments, and leave the head steady thus, and give to the patient dry meat of little moisture so that the limb is comforted and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incising is to look at or open up the head of the abscess, and assemble the point.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for it is never in front;
aucune fois derrier;	never behind;
aucune fois en destre;	never to the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Cut then there where the abscess opens, and the filling of the point, and do according to what you have the power;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and take care that you do not cut the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and let flow a little blood, so that the patient dies from the depletion of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or in the breast, and the disease is ancient, and the medical treatment does not benefit at all, then the last resort cure is the cautery with fire that one uses to cauterize the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It is necessary then, when you cut the veins, that the patient makes his head fall back;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after you rub the spot with a rough cloth as much as the arteries appear, then stretch out the patient's neck under the cloth;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look where the vein beats, and the veins of one and the other are behind the ears, and are a little bent.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then mark the veins of the ankle, then cut one and the other with a sharp instrument in two places, so that the vein reaches just to the bone, and let it be done by the width of the top of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the pointed instrument beneath the artery and cauterize above, cutting just as .ij. fingers deep across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, then the blood constantly flows out above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open to feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then mark the ankle and cut just to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and it is necessary to put blood flow there if it is six ounces, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the replenishment of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if it remains on the bone a point of syphac, if you cut what abscesses burst out from the vein, then hold the wound and bind it, and the treatment of ointment until it is healthy.
de emigrainne	of the migrating (or wandering)
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the migrating pain comes, and catarrh agitates, due to the moisture of the tears and the heat in the temples and old worn-out forehead and similar things, and it is treated by ways of cures of medicine and all that does not profit him, if we extract the arteries from the temples and the cauteries, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes the hairs on their temples grow back, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well with its beating, and is hardly responsive unless in some homes that are too cold;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and when it is responsive, the patient stretches out their neck from some cloth wrappings, then rubs the area with some rough cloth, and raises the area with warm water as much as the artery opens manifestly;
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the spatula-like instrument of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then draw it upwards with pincers, and separate well the tissues that are beneath each part;
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the point of the anvil, then cut according to the quantity of the two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Because she is not cupped, thus she does not jump the blood entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And let blood flow from six lines, just up to three;
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two loops of a strong double silk thread, which prevents bleeding from coming before the sewing of the wound, and prevents blood from flowing;
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then remove the surplus that is between the two ligatures at that hour, and then, if you see fit, cauterize with a cutting cautery up to the bone as long as the head is coped;
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and it is a moderate work, if the patient has no fever and he is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cauterizations are helpful in ending the moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	because it is of great help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries that one fills the cavity with much cotton and places well-made tents;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are dislocated, if they are treated with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with tinctures, until they are healthy;
