et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and without cutting into the artery as much as you observe, if you hasten to do it by cautery, or you apply the virtue of vitriol and hold steady with your hand so the blood is staunched;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you don't have it at hand, put your finger on the spot so the blood is congaled, and raise the spot with cold water until the bleeding stops, and hold steady as it is necessary;
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and that which is more dead and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cautery the vein with this sharp cautery of two edges, but the edge should be well protected to avoid longer delay for the pain.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too hot, they hold less their warmth.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And you should have between the two cuts a space of a large finger's width, and then when you have signed off on both sides, and you pass the burning iron over them until it reaches the bone, and cauterize the vein in both places;
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and let it be separated between the two heads because it is not fully understood from this cautery from start to finish;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that's the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are flowing down into the veins that are on the top of the head, and it does not profit from the cure of medicine that one makes, and you see the face of the patient turning red, and feel the forehead throbbing as if with tremors;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and the eyes are tired and moist as if the hair of the papers is fallen, and the papers are scorched, and burned by the heat of the tears, so it needs this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "contused cure", and it is that you make for the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has on his forehead, then you make three equal incisions on the forehead according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and it be one of the incisions thus as he does all in the front downward to the knee, and the others he has against the ribs, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are against the ribs.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and withdraw your hand from the continuation of the jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers in traversing joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and much of cloth to suck up the blood, then apply the spatula bent to conform to the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	of the incision that is to be made at the temple as far as the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape out all the cartilage that is between the two wounds to the entire siphac which is on the bone, then make another part of the mean incision as far as the other second, and then extract with this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put in the first fissure the instrument that is called "scalpel", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is dull, not very sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the scalpel cutting towards the airy flesh at the heart, and the gentle cut towards the bone, and the cut as far as it reaches the middle seam.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And you will cut the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as far as the incision continues until it reaches what opens in the heart, and then afterwards make a cut in the middle of the fontanelle until the other side.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract the blood equally, and press the limb for the blood taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each fontanelle a tent of old cotton, and put on draped cloths moistened with wine and oil and vinegar, and beware that apostemes do not burst out;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and I will minister great abundance of warm water, then the treatment of anointing with basilicon oil, and other treatments that one uses to cure wounds, until it be healthy.
dou reume des eulz	of the evacuation of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When a vein comes to a customary catharsis, and you see the eyes clouded and small, and the vision is obscured, and the parchments are burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and where the head is in the front it gives pain and anguish, and the patient is exhausted;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you know through these accidents that those matters and this cathartic do not come from many veins, and the mother cure that it is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to shave their forehead, then make a large incision in the forehead, and another just as wide nearby.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the fracture of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be just up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and stretch out your hand from the nerves of the temples that move to the brain;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then separate between the two lips of the fracture and put much cotton, and tighten with linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then lay on top moistened cloths in wine and oil, and beware of a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is put back, it is necessary that you rub the bone so that flesh begins to grow, then treat with excitant things that make flesh grow.
En teil maniere:	In such a manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of flour of wheat, and of colofonia four parts, and make an emplaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it to these wounds to heal quickly everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	either grains, or beast, or rock from a mine or similar thing, just like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, as in vetches, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things, such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When the bone grows in the pierced ear or another manner of thing that does not join to the ear, and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then distill no drop of violet oil or oil of sisament, then administer extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make the condition stern, and stop up the nostrils when the sternum comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and hold the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times relief comes through this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, then one should try extracting with subtle pincers, because that is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes out with the pincers, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then one should try extracting with a subtle hook of small double curvature;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out by that, then make a cane of iron and insert the tip of the cane into the perforation of the ear strongly, and block what is around the cane with wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then one draws out in a regular form, because many times relief comes if we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in that manner, then take glue from where one takes the bones, and put some instrument that is pointed for doing that, and put a little cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the gut against the stone or whatever it is, and pull strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not burst forth from all these things that we have said, then hasten to open the ear thus, and abscess will flow out, and spasm;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of the opening is that you first make the patient with a head wound healthy, and extract blood according to the measure of its virtue, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small opening at the root of the ear at the fat or depending on it;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the opening be as wide as a moon, until you reach the stone, then scrape according to your power, and suck hastily into your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if there are grains that are inside and they swell, then administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if he cannot issue, if you handle the spatula subtly according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision into that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do it when you think that the grains are moist because of the moisture in the ear, so much that you have made many parts;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with subtle pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is alleviated.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case where it falls into the ear, it is necessary that the patient uses the discharge of condenser first, and fills the ear with much cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it be placed on that same ear where the pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it gets worse from that point, it's bad.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, take many pairs according to the length of your fingers, and hold them lightly, and warm them a little at the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put the patient's one or pierced ear on it, and elevate it above his feet from another side, and make a hole of another stone on the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease to make this from stone to stone as long as the water issues forth completely, and thus it will flow completely forth;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, if you take the joint, and put one of the heads in the ear, and the other head takes fire until the most tender joint is burnt;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then redo another part of the joints until the water issue is all out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as it is a pimple and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large body that one can feel it, then prepare an extraction of forceps;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and where you treat the distillations, and the cure does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you examine the ear in the sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If it opens into void spaces, if they draw them out with subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, take the candle of what is its form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the most subtle instrument into the ear according to the quantity of the sufferer's pain, then suck formally throughout the candle.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do it often so that all the veins appear.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to issue out, stop up the candle with cotton as I have said in the stone.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not issue forth as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have experienced in the operation of the veins, and you will find them or treat with distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and your medicines into the ear through this entire instrument, from which is its form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let it be of silver or of copper, spread underneath to the small openings, and above spread out to distill.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press within the distillation the copper instrument well-made for that, and if you see take the receiver and envelop it around the tip of the cotton-covered point.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then you pour your oil or your juice, and that which you take from your medicines in the reed, and let the reed be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then thrust into the receiver all the cotton, and press your hand temporarily so that the oil is distilled or flows out of the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels it within, and let the distillations be a little warm from the fire in this way so that it is distilled into the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and beware that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be good if it were.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have some hole in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men through swelling of wounds, or a born-in abscess within the ear, and these swellings sometimes come in deeply into the ear, if one cannot see it well;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes it happens that the small hole is closed, and one sees it very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes in deeply, if one cannot see it, is a grievous sore in many conditions, and in that which one sees, it is necessary that you put the ear of the patient in the sunlight;
et regarde dedens:	and look within:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the opacity appearing, so that the work has all this spatula-like material from which it is formed:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, all smooth, so that it does not blister the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the operation is on a new or raw flesh of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers and cover lightly, so that all the flesh is fully opened.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operations are deep in the ear, take a subtle, light razor and heat it slightly by fire, then place it in the course of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the operation where the patient feels great pain at the ear, touch lightly and be careful not to disturb the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and apply it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do nothing for several days until the wound is suppurated, or take a tent and apply it with rose water, and powder with pulverized vitriol.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear inflamed, it is necessary that you remove the tent and apply another tent coated with a mixture of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is gone.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal him until he is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a flow of blood comes, soak an sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the flow of blood which are treating with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papyra (paper-like skin)
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	These are the ulcers that come in papers of eyes when they are moist and dry, if it is necessary that you treat them with tongs and tweezers, and cover with a spatula of their roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on the place a vitriol ointment.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it does not peel off, then the subtle lenticular fire cautery, and the cautery man is worth more after the incision.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times they repair, as long as nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the scab
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times there come in papers of eyes some things that seem fat in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	take warning that the joint moves from one side to another, and it's a light thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	make the wound somewhat large, then scrape the skin of each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and cover it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot cover it without piercing a little the paper, do not harm anything to the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the fracture is large, assemble it with a bandage, and care for it until it is healthy;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not use force, for the joints restore themselves quickly and do harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the joint is deep inside the ear towards the upper part, reverse the paper, and stretch the joint with pincers, and cover and press from one side to another;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the skin is separated by incision, it does not hurt at all;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the artery is cut, if you lift the eye of salt water, and heal the limb of those who are injured in such a way that the patient may be healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fatness that is inflamed in the membranes of the skin above, and this happens more to infants than to old people, and hurts much their eyes, and they come to have catarrh in the mornings, and cannot gaze at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this they lay their faces down again, and sleep on them, and their skin is beneath their eyebrows moist which the inflammation and appearance have covered with the exinach that opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand against your arm and feel the numbness entering within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the surgery is such that the patient puts their head in a healthy position;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take the linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that each part contains, then place it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the skin is gathered together within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make a milestone of the moisture at the cutting edge, making a cut as large, and not more than the wound that one makes in the vein's sinew;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin deep enough so that you reach the skin;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many arrangements comes the skin from the cut, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then pull away a piece of cloth firmly between your fingers at the defect, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread out;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and beware that you do not push into the crack, that you do not come to the entire spatula just up to the eye, that you do not bruise it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the extremity does not open at the beginning of the crack, then increase it a little more lightly so that it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then wrap in oil and in water, and put on the limb, and hold with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break their own arm and put it back to correct the moisture that has gone bad.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the arm, then treat it with soothing ointments until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When in papers hairs are wrongly aligned other than naturally, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes, and bring on ways of illnesses such as customary tears and softening of the papers and albumen, so that it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and it is the treatment according to three manners:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	where by fire cautery, or by medicinal agua according to what is before or chapter of cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on your healthy side, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is converted, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	see that not, if you push a needle to the thread above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be along the edge of the paper where the hairs grow from these hairs, and draw the thread above to the entire paper, and turn it to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part below the paper, below the aligned hairs, to the entire spatula coping, from the large lantern up to the small;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and place under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then sign on the paper a figure of an inch, like the leaf of myrtle, and however it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevated the paper which is divided into toes.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if you have a part that is master of the craft, take a large quantity of paper according to how much the paper is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make all spatula-shaped on the two lines that you have signed, and begin with a large lantern just up to small.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the onion in one of the two angles of the heel, then scrape everything.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips to a stitch of a needle with all the subtle thread of flax, and suck out the blood, and make straight the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows at all gluey things, if you want to do this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if it does not work, then abandon the treatment, and leave the stitches and threads until three or four days.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then cure the wound without tight constricting things, because the skin revives at the suddenness of the wound and its assembly, but the constricting is muted (as the ancient said), and it's work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another manner:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you shape the skin into a figure that is as if the leaf of myrtle, as we have related, at three ounces of scarification according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then apply to those who have small equal forces in harmony with the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, take a needle or it has one thread, and put it in the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put another thread from the large lantern, and the second thread from the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have related, then assemble the two lips of the wound by constricting, and cure until it is healthy;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm the angry swelling with similar gentle touches.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the parchment are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if it is necessary, you should use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of wounds is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you convert the parchment and make them inside according to what I have said, and then make two wounds by art, and two subtle links as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut as two heads of two parts or you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly above what overflows from the parchment of the eye, and stretch out the two wounds of the two parts fully;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it thus for some days, and the skin that is constrained will become numb and weak, and porous, until it falls apart by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, if it resists to some forces, then cure it until it is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sewn, and if the paper is lifted, and they will not prick the hairs anymore;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and it is the form of the two canals that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the operations are such that you take a subtle needle, and you thread a soft and subtle silk thread;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the heads and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm's length;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and tie the two heads of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's head in a healthy position;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be exposed to the sun so that the operations may be clarified, for this is a subtle and minor operation, then insert the needle at the root of the hair being treated, and make it pierce the paper hastily until you draw it above the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then extract the hair up to the root, and put into the root that hair, if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then extract your hand so that the hairs come forth from the root in the paper along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the root is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then pull the root downwards along the entire thread that you had ordained, so that the root comes forth from the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you should thread the bow and the filament, and close the eye and let it stay closed for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh begins to form.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are small, accompany the long hair of the natural whiskers, and be elevated with that or you leave it, until it is elongated and then set free.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purification of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the porridge comes into the eye, if there are two manners of it:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from a blow, or from a cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of operating on it is that you sew up the wound, and separate the lips of it, and put in threads of linen, and leave it until it be healthy;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not suitable that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	Because if you do this, the disease will return worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but I observe things that soothe, as in fenugrec;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose water or alta and linseed oil should be heated, and ointments of dyaquilon melted into one of the oils, and I enveloped a tent, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your cure is that you take heed that it does not sink according to the form it was in beforehand;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and this work that we have said is not stronger than the symptoms of this disease, so that it does not relapse according to the form it was in beforehand.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is disfigured, truly named "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wounds and fractures and cauterization and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of the work in this is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and fix it in the flesh, and make it pierce from the left arm to the right, so that the thread comes out at the head of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then the flesh is above all the spine, and the coping to the spatula is wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the skin returns according to what it needs, that's good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, then take the rasp and put it in the fissure, and turn the skin, and make two fissures or sew within the skin;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and be the heads of the two fissures at the two angles of the incision that you have coped, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is just like the shape of a letter which is not "I griesche";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh, according to the quantity whose edges are agreed upon below, from what follows the skin, then adjust the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the treatment with those softening medications that we have mentioned, and tents, until it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a crack or a stitch or a burn, then it is necessary that you make a plain crack beneath the hairs of the papers, and according to what is here before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to be ingenious in every way so that they can make the figure return to its natural shape;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the same patients, according to what is necessary for the work and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	because of the burning of the parchment
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this join has to be made in such a way that the paper above is stuck with the white of the egg, and cannot move or do its natural work, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor beneath the paper, and lift it high;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and hold the pincers, as long as you grasp what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too pointed nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer that the spatula is too pointed and does not bleed the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and make your incision, where you scrape off the assembled one lightly, so that the skin regains its natural shape;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it is healthy throughout the assembled one, and they never make salty aqueous humor in the eye, and they raise sweet watery discharge, and from the collar bone;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put between the skin and eye a linen bandage, and place on the eye a wet linen cloth in abundance of egg whites;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day, use sweet collar bone and things that follow, until it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and resembles the hardness of a firm, dry cord, and another which is not nervous, but resembles the softness of a moist, congealed blain, that when touched with iron and cut with pinces, it cannot be removed;
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and one and the other resemblance begins towards the large artery, and grows little by little until it covers all vision and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts their head in a healthy position, then they open their eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper with your hand, then bend the finger into small doubles, and stretch it out above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and insert the hair of a horse, or of a cow, or of an ox, and pull it strongly;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and stick it in the ankle, and pierce all the way through the needle, and tie the ankle with a thread and hold it from above, and scrape off all the hair on the side of the ankle that connects the prune and the skin to the hair just at the head, then cut the remaining part into the root of the arm at all subtle and small forces, and let the natural flesh or arm, so that by incision do not disturb the course of the tears accustomed.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes it happens that the ankle is held back by the oncine alone, and with a thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then scrape off all the subtle skin where it is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And beware that the subtle skin does not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the prune does not perforate;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, pour a little of warm broth into the oil, and make a poultice with it from litharge, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat what is necessary so that it may be healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push the needle, and the veins cannot enter, often this type of nail is cured by medications;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and it grows thus as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, if you open the oil of the patient, and take the spatula lightly a little gently according to this form;
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And raise the nail subtly, and if you see that it diminishes to a point and the reason presses on, then distill from your mouth into the oil made with litharge and red copper and warm broth, and stop up the oil until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then resume the other work according to this same method, so that it is all ordered.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to the eye, then as an aposteme heats up, then milk it, and first cure the hot aposteme until it is healthy, then restart the treatment as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh wounds at night with great annoyance, if it suspects in the ankle, and cuts into one part and not entirely, that course of tears does not come;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill in the eye a red collar which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	It is the eyes of some men that never saw red flesh, and covers the prunella and holds back on the papers and turns to the deceiver, and resembles a rose of baluster.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the works are such that the patient puts his head in your healthy tone, then he opens his eyes, and gathers all that flesh as convenient joints to that, and holds it with force;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then cut the first flesh, and go all cutting to the raspier until the end, and beware that you do not blind the eye at the work;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and it is the incision of a spatula-like tool that we have mentioned in the incision of the ankle and with small forces, because one should loosen the swelling as the form shows after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is accomplished and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of a broiet seed or you distill coliere rouge and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil a layer of cotton with a stream of egg white, so that it be assured against a hot abscess.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it remains nothing, and the blood flows excessively, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing things that calm a hot abscess.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work as long as it is healthy, and thus make sure that the flesh is adjusted in the oil by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	However it is necessary that you adjust the treatment according to the natural weakness of each oil.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental way, in the work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	from the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	There are veins that are red and covered on the eye, and take away its function and obscure the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary therefore at first that you examine the oil, in which the patient is afflicted, it is outside, and there is no other disease except the outer one.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then the coil in such a manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in your healthy one, then suspend those veins all around according to his wisdom, and let the subtle double onions be according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be an eleven-inch incision by degrees in this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then you should coil the veins subtly with force, and suck out the blood hourly after another, until you see that you are removing those outer veins from the oil.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and beware that you do not blind the eye at the points of the spatula, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not seize except those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then distill into the eye a green and red collirium to corrupt what is dormant due to the evil of the belly.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are not able to collect all this at that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of soothing things to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is alleviated and assured of hot abscess, then resume according to this manner which is before until it be healthy;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and that is the form of the fractures:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The mirror, thus named "arissati", a fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you treat with fire cautery and with ardently burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not without health, if there is an abscess within which you make an incision, there where it should be drained, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and blackness, if you take away all the instruments of which it is the form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "rough head", and let it be made into an iron instrument at the rough head, and let it be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put on the rough bone of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the rough bone with excitatory medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the eyes are inflamed, and there is a burning sensation, and the body of the bowel is inflamed, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not improve and is not apostematous, and bad accidents come to pass, showing that it is unhealthy.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If this does not work, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the hole of the nostril according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you discover the bone for the second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it has been discovered, take the forest according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and the fistula should be attenuated up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone of the injured arm, and separate your hand from the eye of the hole, then turn all the forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by this means that the veins come into being if he holds his hand against his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the limbs, thus goes the material to the nail;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open everywhere, and it does not come to disturb the nail, nor diminish, thus it is necessary that you read the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the vein, then apply ventouses or a hot iron without piercing to suck, then put on the eye a linen cloth made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then hold the eye, and bind it with strips and drapery;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the way of the strips is that you take strips quite soft, and fold each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then hold it back above a hardened bandage, forming a shape, and reapply the cupping glasses to suck out the infected matter without piercing the skin.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the cupping glasses and hold the eye steady day and night, and if the veins are swollen, it is necessary that you extract a lot.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the vein after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, it's good.
se ce non;	If not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you reapply the plaster and the bandages and the vein and the cupping glasses until he is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	because of the tearing of a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When cracks appear in the web-like membrane, then open, and issue forth fragments like grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see the web-like membrane, the operations are such that you insert a needle at the root of the affected part below, then insert another needle where it has a double thread from the part of the arm.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and have them pierce, and leave the first needle according to its disposition;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then thread the eye of the double file, and tie one part of the tube around it, and hold it well, then remove the needle and place it on the same moistened spot in abundance of egg whites;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it be until the thread absorbs with the egg whites, then heal the eye with comforting things until the wound is healthy;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and often the wound is held in place by a piece of cloth in a circle, until it is healed.

puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the hollow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a swelling that is assembled in the eye, appearing as if it were dripping, and this is not really dripping;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of the appearance of the disease is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and upright, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it so that you see the swelling come up to your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then be fixed, and do not bend down and be disordered in the light, and see the patient's things as if he were alone;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is dripping, and the descents of the swelling are not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and touch the corner of the horn-like tissue by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horn-like tissue and the crown, until the swelling subsides;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is dislocated, if you distill into the hot oil mixed with honey, or hot oil or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then it should be treated with another treatment until it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	from the corners of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have the similarities of the hot oils in the division, and this is what is necessary to pierce;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if it operates according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and bind the healthy oil strongly and tightly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the paper of the oil in your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if the eyes are on the right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are on the right;

et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measurement of the way of almagda be at the forefront of the measurement of the spaces which are from the prunelle just up to the end of the blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and it is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the horny tissue, and then place the instrument just where the water is, then press it down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Here is the translation:
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting a little, and if the water rises by the second way, place the strength with the instrument, and when it is thus fixed and does not mount, then extract almagda lightly by turning your hand little by little.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back in water a small gemstone, and lift from it the eye within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then puts by default the eyes stupefied or clouded with rose oil and in abundance of egg whites, and mixes it with healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on common broth with an abundance of egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which is the form.

et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not suitable that you do this in the hour of the treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you elevate it, because the water mounts quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	Here is the translation:
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is alleviated, if he dislocates the view and puts his face in the mirror to cover any flaw, and so then it is in that dark house.

et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Iraq, who told us that in his country they made a certain alumgaude powder, which attracts the water, but meanwhile I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.

de la char sor le neis	from the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Never grow or produce various diverse char marks, from which there are some that resemble scorptions on the foot.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there is such a mark or a char with an enhanced fixed color, and if it has a soft char of a bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that case of those chars which are soft and not enhanced, you should make the patient sit between your hands against the sun.

Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, open it completely with the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains.

et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize them until the blood is stanched and all the flesh is burned away, then apply either oil or water or wine.

et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not pass as it suits, know that there is new flesh growing in the bone above, for which the instruments do not come to cut;
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then it is necessary that you put a thread of linen, somewhat thick, and sew with our hands, and have between each stitch of space a doit or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's head in the noose of the thread at his nose as it suits, and pull gently until it comes through the nose into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times they act like a child in school, it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes by the nose to one hand, and the other head that comes by the mouth to the other hand, and let them follow each other in being sound as we who are or were.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this as much as you know that the nodes have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, suck out the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian oil, and put it back in place as before.

et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on the nose a plaster of lead for several days until it is healthy, and if there is need of dry medications, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and it is the shape of the instrument for purging the head, where they distill oils and medicines or not:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	Whether of silver or copper, resembling an overturned lamp, like a chain, and the conduits thus;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, make a closed chain, and let the instruments be flat for purging the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and hold the handle to the head to keep it still when one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a tumor grows on the head which is called "telul", and it increases and becomes large again, until it is a visible thing to behold;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason you must cut into the tumor at the beginning, and clear out everything, then put on top the cautery or the burning medicine;
