et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay cutting until it is large, take care if it is hard, of fixed color, of poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not touch the iron with your hand because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you touch it sometimes, great evil comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of fixed color, and you see that one can cover it completely, if you examine the patient and touch it without fear, and heal the place with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is affected and ulcerated
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when continuous solutions come into one of these cartilaginous openings, it profits little, because in some homes.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is necessary therefore to see if it has reached none, if you look at the wound to see if it is fresh in all its blood.
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bring the two lips of the wound together with a suture, then heal it until it is healthy;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their skin until they heal, then bring the two lips together with a suture, and hold them in place, and sprinkle powder made from dragon's blood, and incense broiet;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place on the poultices a piece of plaster of strong or another plaster suddenly, and let it stick to him, then heal the joint so that it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the fracture is that you assemble the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the fracture of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	At times men have within their lips hard abscesses, similar to grains of peas, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and split on each nut, and take them as pincers and cut into each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the remedy afterwards, after the incision of vitriol broth, until the wound is stained;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the oil of iris, and heal the wound with dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the decay of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often it happens beneath the gums where it is pressed, which the ancient ones call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	it is necessary that you hold it as in tongs, and cut at its root, and let the blood or sap flow;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then apply on the affected place a glassy powder, or other drying and constricting powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it returns after the incision, and often happens, then cut a second time, and cauterize;
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of the abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are laid and pressed;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes they are black, yellow, and green teeth, as long as the decay reaches the gum, and the teeth are putrid;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	it is necessary that you seat the patient between your hands, and their head be in your holy, and take the teeth or the scars appearing, until there remains nothing.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make of the blackness and the greenness, and of the yellowness and the other stains, until they are wiped away.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes that which is at the first rash, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then recommence to re-treat on the second day and the third, until you have everything ready.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth have need of diverse forms of instruments for extraction, according to what the work demonstrates, because the roots that one extracts from the teeth have other forms than those that one extracts between the teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others be with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat a tooth with its pain that you delay to handle it as much as you can, for this must not be done hastily.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance just up to then so that one has no excuse to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to receive treatment, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth that hurts.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a sound tooth, and makes them handle the good tooth;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and always the pain does not depart from that, as much as the bad one is extracted, for we have already wanted to do it to these healthy ones;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are very certain of the tooth that is hurting, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides, strongly plying the gum with a spatula to ward off from all parts;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it with your fingers or subtle nails at the first little by little, until it is well loosened, then firmly affix the nails.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient be in your holy hand between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each part lightly, and you remove it just like you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the teeth are pierced and gnawed, it is necessary that you fill them with cloth, there where the holes are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you hold it subtly in the tendons, so that it does not break while holding.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to operate very carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you do well to beware that you do not break it, and leave a part remaining, and reveal to the patient by the wickedness of the root more great pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeon, who through their haste and hardness often break the cartilage, and do not amend what we have recounted.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but they often come through the examination of this great illness for the roots that remain, or for the cartilage that they break, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is extracted, you wash the jaw with wine or vinegar and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and we stop the bleeding that comes, which often happens, by applying the juice of bruised vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if it does not heal, you should cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the instruments, which you should blunt first, so they are at long points and thick handles, so they do not slip when you extract the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large limbs so they do not bend in the traction, and let them be of iron well-made, and let them be toothed to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the socket, it is necessary that you place on the jaw a cotton cloth soaked in borax or butter I day or II, as long as the gums are softened, then you apply the tongs called "algefri", from which the head seems to be a beak of a sign.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they should be made thus, like a file, and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to issue from all these pincers, then it is necessary that you discover the flesh entirely surrounding the root, and he puts on the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a palate scraper, from which this is their form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so it does not break, and if its roots spring forth from that, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If that's not so, help with all the instruments, because of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has several grooves, from which the form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front of the dens' ratio, and of this instrument that resembles large pincers, from which the form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong so they cannot break, and know that many of these dense instruments are.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters subtly find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the diseases show them, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach about instruments due to the diversity of wounds; and one breaks a part of the cartilage or other bones, or it becomes porous, if they seek those instruments that they need, which I have told you, and help with gestures, from which this form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let it be thick and holding well to hold the bone, so it does not slip away, but it can hold and ostend.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the limb with suitable medications for this, and if it has porous bone, and it is small, so take into account all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the natural body, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, so it is necessary that you know if the teeth are not after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot solder or file:
adonques lou raie;	then the root;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument which has the shape, and is similar to a small beak, and let it be of iron sharp in the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping is little by little in the morning hours for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file with a similar file as its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file with which one makes the needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in a gentle manner, little by little, he puts his teeth together gradually, so that it does not move until it settles.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the flat surface at the end of everything without any roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and they bite the tongue, it is necessary to file the asperity until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth falls out, either by shock or by decay, and the patient cannot press on it because it hurts, and you treat them with constricting medications, but it is of no value.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	it is necessary to hold them back with a thread of gold, because the silver thread turns green and decays, but the gold does not move at all.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the threads be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you want to realign the teeth, take the thread and double cord between the healthy teeth, then put the heads between the crooked teeth, even if there is one or more, until you straighten them right up to the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then reestablish the covering right up to the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and steadily, so that it does not move at all;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the heads of the thread at a small nail, and assemble them, and put them back between the healthy tooth, and set it so that it does not touch the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then leave it tightly in place as long as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the threads break, hold it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it delays and serves thus all its tension, and it is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and of the two muscles, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if you replace it in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not intervene with those who are not wise and suffer, and never make the form of a tooth from an ivory tusk, and put it in the place where the defect is, and hold it steady as we have said, and delay and serve thus long tension.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the thread of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never is this bond that comes from under the tongue or naturally, which one is born with;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accidental wound suddenly;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the operations are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your healthy one, and lift the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then cut the nervous thread as long, until the tongue is dislocated from its hold, and if there is hardness or numbness, and it's a sudden wound, if you cut the uncleanness and cut as long that binds.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and beware that the fissure is not too deep in the front, because of the artery which is underneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done it, lift up the level of warm water and of hazel, or of cold water, then place underneath the tongue a tent of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and touch the patient's gum each night, so that the levels cannot become swollen.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if a flow of blood comes, then place on the level a vitriol poultice;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the wound does not heal, then cauterize it with a slow-burning cauter, which is good for that;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Then the treatment of another treatment as long as he is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see that the abscess is of a foul color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it declines to a whitish color, and there is moisture, so he throws in the onion, and makes an ointment of a subtle spatulum, and delivers from one part and another.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the blood does not come to your work, so put on a glassy broth as long as it is stained, then return to your work as much as you treat everything fully.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then raise the level of vinegar and of oil, and the treatment of other treatments as long as he is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes there come within the throat ulcers that are called "godath", and they are properly called the II abscesses, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, take heed.
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is abscesses hard of little sense and of fused color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron, also for the deterioration of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it becomes ripe, and then you will divide it, where it would break by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color returning, and the root is subtle, then have the instrument ready to cut, but first see that the abscesses are calm and appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head be in your hand, and open their mouth and take the scissors between their hands, and press the tongue beneath all the instrument, so that it is in the form;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and let it be of silver or of subtle iron also as a kind of knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue against this instrument, and you see the abscess, if you take the onion and place it in the amulet, and make the trajectory flow above more than you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and draw nothing from the tiles with it, then cover the instrument, because it is the shape, which seems like a force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all ways the head is curved, and one end to the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or of steel;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, take a candle with tongs, because it is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And it is cutting on one side, and named on the other side;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have covered one of the amulets, if you cover the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and hot and dry, and if there is evacuation of blood, then gargle the patient with hot water, or scorching of green pomegranates which are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is stanched;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then let the wound heal until it is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and another time abscesses do not grow in the throat besides the two mandibles, if they are treated thus like the two mandibles are treated.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I medically treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, it is to know the small abscess of little sense;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had almost closed off her entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the constricted passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high up that it had pushed through two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then, and made an incision in one of the tonsils, then the flow of pus was abundant, and a large portion of it poured out.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I made another incision in the other perforation of the nose, and I opened the mouth and pressed on the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After making an incision in these abscesses, and cutting into a part, only a little blood comes out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And then the woman's throat constricted, and now she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting into that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscesses grew back again, and filled the void that I had emptied, so much that it became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Then I deceived him and cauterized inside his throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Then he waited without growing worse;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I left those regions, and knew only that God did it afterwards.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the humors descend to the womb, and it is inflamed and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is swollen and round, then it is called "womb".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit at all, and you see that the ulcerous abscess is alleviated, and it is subtle, so it is necessary that you cauterize it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one that is rounded and gathered, and is not lengthy;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is blood-red or of a dark color or black, so it is necessary that you avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then prick the onion in the urine, and extract it from beneath, and cauterize with one of the two instruments that I have said for incising the two veins.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not operate more fiercely than the surplus which is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you operate more, it harms the voice, and the speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two handles, and cure it until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about operating, it is necessary that you use gentleness in the cautery of the senses for fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of burning by cautery is sharp and bitter.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts their head in your healthy hand, and then presses their tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confirms with living water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using the handling of this instrument, from which there is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have on the head a hair or where one puts the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument to apply all the medicine onto the wound;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And the patient should be leaning on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth to the medicine inside, so that it does not descend into the throat, and the blister.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then put your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the eye, for a quarter of an hour, until you see the inflammation and the bites of the medicine are alleviated.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around an instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and apply the instrument to all the affected area above, until the cotton adheres onto the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this frequently, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and expect to see results after three or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have need to restart the cauterization of the medicine, then restart it, and after cauterizing, clean around the eye with cotton dipped in boric acid, and clarify what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let there be risen from cold water, and let there be cured of garglings as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than incision, not that the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	it is cured of fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put it in a gentle heat, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and in the pot has an instrument prepared in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And let it be of silver or of copper, and let one of the heads be thrust into the patient's mouth as long as the vapors rise to the eye through the cane, so that the eye is mortified;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the remedy is repeated often, until the eye dries out, and be careful that you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of the hot abscess, for many things happen there;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make a bigger wound than at the decline of an abscess's fall.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not available, take a cane and place a thread of egg white in the chief's head, so that the patient's mouth does not burn too much;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the egg white thread does not let the bad vapor hurt the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether for salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it happens to have an obstruction in the throat or spine of a fish, or some other thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is necessary that you extract what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing clearly;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit thus, so that the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance if he vomits the bitter thing
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	where the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and there is a thread on the sponge, and then it passes through;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the place, if it sticks, and then you will draw out strongly;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out from what we have said, take the instrument of a probe according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can enter more lightly into the throat, and hold the head high and lifted;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all comes out, and do not push the bone within;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows when the thing is bitter;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If you apply heat below, or if you pull it out completely with the instrument evenly, so that it is straight.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the sensitivity of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No medicine is effective, as I said in the section, through the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not benefit, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument as I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the bruise, take it all to the small inch, or with subtle tendons that come to this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a curled hair, and put it in the patient's throat, then put or make the curl of the hair into a hot iron, and make it sweat.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And tease the patient with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take full sight of cold water, and open the mouth, and let it glide in sensibly, and move it with its own hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if the patient soon feels the water, he recovers.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if he does not recover as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asphalt, to the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the womb;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall more gently.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are visible charcoal bits, and it should be covered with a perforated sheet in the middle, and in this pierced one should be the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you throw in the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes just to the sanies;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the sanies will now purge, and if they do not purge, then recommence the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient sweat, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink any water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then the liver will be cleansed by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument through which one draws the sanies is such that when one can see it, it resembles curved tongs for drawing mucus into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it has resemblance to a healthy nose, and it has roughness of lime, so that what she takes, she cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and see there the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the surgeons of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many similarities of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings here after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and in size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners, of which one is in its own resemblance, and because of what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is by means of the eyes or where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the body are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if there are abscesses that one must not pierce, as long as the bowel is ripe according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are on the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves them until they are ripe on the outside, perhaps because the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is on a principal limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will injure the principal limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	where it is of the foundation, if one pierces thus so that it dies;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not suitable that you pierce an abscess without complete digestion, unless it is of the foundation, so that it does not putrefy within, and is lengthened, and a fistula forms;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which dies according to completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the departures from the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and of the redness, and the debating and adjusting of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make a hole for the perforation or more depending on the abscess, and where it opens badly;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and it is the perforation of a long wound in the body, and if the abscesses are in his hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equal places where there is no putrefaction.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, they complain, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh, it is better that you let the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce before that, so the body is poisoned by his own venom, and it is full of much filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps they harden the lips and the depths of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the members need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you diminish small abscesses, small perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many fissures according to the appearance of the greatness of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the skin, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become so like a drape, and is mortified, if it is necessary to do as one does with pimples;
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are those that one covers thus like the foil of myrtle, thus as abscesses of the loins;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, thus as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce them plainly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected great pus, and you pierce them, so do not drain all the pus at that hour, but drain a part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then staunch the abscess until another day, then drain nothing further there;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times, little by little, until all the pus has been drained;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	meanwhile the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the surgeon operates too hastily with the flow of pus, which by chance kills the patient, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Here is the translation:
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a flat wound, you should apply tinctures of flax or cotton wool;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, you should put a tent in each one so that they meet each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of soft skin, and you have shaved around it, you should fill it with old cotton or a dressing of linen threads without moisture, and leave it just to the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then anoint it, and treat it with ointment until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you remove blood that has come to the surface during your work, if you calm down the agitated and anxious, and soothe the inflamed area, and put a dressing on the wound that is healing many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the blood deterioration persists, you should apply government and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in my book, and if it is a winter condition, and the joints or abscess are very nervous, you should put on tents and moist drapes soaked in warm wine and oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in this state, and the limbs are numb, then it is necessary that you apply warm drapels to the affected area with water and oil, or with wine and oil mixture, until the third day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open up the abscess and the wound and the treatment, as it is necessary, until he is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And it is necessary to thoroughly know how to treat abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	as I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where there are small abscesses coming from the head, and they are ways of ours that are in veils, just like the juice of a hazelnut, and much has been seen with similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and such as those where there is moisture, just like pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are some that are hard and stony at the cutting, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the cutter are such that you experience with every instrument that is called "incision", from which the form comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it flows out above the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, then scrape off everything without leaving the skin that contains this moisture, for it returns immediately when you leave nothing.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then thrust a cotton swab into an Egyptian injection, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	But this not, in a pointed instrument and in silk, and fill the wound, and let it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and they run through that which is hardened by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then reinsert the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not harden by night.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound of injection with this convenient method, until it be healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscesses hold in a thick knot, then cut according to this form, from afar.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and you scrape the onions, and remove the scab from all parts, and put all your treatment of drawing forth for the quotidian fever where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery does the opposite, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus do for the abscess if it is pierced, and on cutting and on curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the pierced abscess and the moist, it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if there are some of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and it was one of the abscesses that I treated on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess was like a stone, rough and whitish, and could not be broken;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had touched any of it, one would have done as much harm as to a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming on the head, because those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, one must open so that it may be most dependent on the location, in order to issue forth the pus;
et les cure si com il covient.	and the treatment should be as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of the scalps
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times the abscess forms on the neck, and beneath the shoulders, and in the loins, and sometimes it comes to another part of the body, and they are numerous, and are entangled one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its side, just like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the similarities of these ulcerations are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that then you see of good disposition in the touching, and it is similar to the color of the flesh, and changes from each part and is not at all airy as near the neck nor in the artery, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if it is necessary that you cut through above, and scrape the skin from each part, and stretch the two lips of the heart as oncines, if you are a master, as we have said in abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and pull gently and little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not let the spatula slip, lest the hand fail, and do not push too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not stop bleeding, then put on the wound a vitriol ointment, or some powders that staunch blood, and hold the wound fast.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it be until the abscesses are softened, and the wound is soothed, and begin to make it putrefy.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stagnant, return to your work, until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then seek with your finger if there remain small scrophulae, if they gather and multiply.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is in the root of the vein a large scrophula, it does not behoove that you cut that scrophula at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with much cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, then treat.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire abscess, it is necessary that you reassemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there will be no more superfluity due to the greatness of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cut at the root of it, and draw out fiercely, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrophulae that hold a surplus, pierce them there where they appear most tender.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce them thus as the one mentioned before, depending on it, then I will treat them with oil and similar things, so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, if the treatment of anointing is done skillfully, so that it may be healthy.
de squinance	of bruising
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	They used to say and talk about the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and it's the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have a hoarse voice, it is necessary that the partition of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cleared;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one should not help by that alone, because all the veins and the breathing of the patient are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the mandrels.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the purging, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the destruction that comes from the strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it beneath three circles or four a small cut across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the syphac, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and they must be careful at the section of the epiglottis that there is no spot of flesh, and the vessels are long of inquiry.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the masters are afraid, it is necessary that they stretch the skin of the throat all around the tonsils, then cut through the cartilage as far as it reaches the uvula;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and clear the blood vessels, if you see nothing, and then cut through the syphac, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the tube of the uvula which is forced out by the broken voice, and by the defect of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a little.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound at the neck, and sew it entirely without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that make flesh grow, so it may be healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	One must not do this just as long as the throat is completely stuffed, and the patient is judged to death, and the default gives up the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then operate on the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and by this command the old man left the wound open so that the evil of the disease would pass, and it passed in three days or four; And then he commanded to cauterize the wound and cure, so that it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took the knife, and she placed it in her throat, and cut part of the sinews of her arm;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and I found her almost dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that it had not been properly covered, neither vein nor artery, and the veins were issuing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and cured her so that she was healthy;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and he did not have at the young woman's fever when she was hoarse of voice, and recovered afterwards to her condition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I know that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	These abscesses are called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a jasmine, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	where naturalness has no point of obstruction.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, one of which resembles a fatty tumor to us, and the other manner resembles an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is no fear, and it does not want to open a false flow except in the one that is small, and it proves and searches throughout the entire introgression;
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it thus, as I grasp nothing, and do not find in any vein, if it is covered, if as we cover the nuts, and draw to its entire coffin, if there is no point;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and investigate well everywhere, and heal it as it is fitting, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of wounds, which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now it is fitting that I tell all the difference that is between wound and injury.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that injury is heat and fever holding, until the inflammation has passed, and it is accompanied by putridity.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then set aside the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the wound there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins thus as a boil, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to the second similarities, whether grayish, or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the ninth node, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to what its form will be or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inspecting the abscesses of the nails is that you press or make the skin more moist than you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, so that you know that the strumens have perceived the heart, then it is according to the greatness of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the suppuration, and take heed in this, that it bursts forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture flows out, whatever its color may be, thus it is done as I have said about the other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the suppuration no moisture comes, know that it is fat, thus do it in a cross, and take it with pincers, and lightly scrape each part and turn the skin where it lies, so that you draw it out whole with the knot.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it straight, pull it by pieces so that there remains nothing.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if it remains nothing, then it returns to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it remains a little, and the wound does not grieve you, then apply to the wound some corrosive powders, and hold the wound steady, and put on soothing abscess treatments hot, and treat with other treatments until it is healthy;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat what is injuring flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein is throbbing against you or otherwise, then hasten and apply the liquid of broken vitriol, and let it stay two or three days, until the wound suppurates, and restore the ebullition of blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cauterizing what has remained of the tumor.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the forms of inward-turned instruments, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large, moderate, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, moderate, and small, for enclosing the abscesses of a fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one cuts the sorcels, and they are of citrus iron, or of iron, or of silver, and those that are yellow are more proven for enclosing the abscesses of a fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, moderate, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the lancets are very similar, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, moderate, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if there are eleven which have three deformities in three ways thus;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are eleven which have three deformities, and they are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are eleven which have two deformities, and eleven with only one deformity, and they are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these is sharp to the point where they are cut, and there are those that do not cut except for one part, from which the nails are scraped, because one does not touch the vein nor the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these introjections are the humors collected in the hands, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and gentle, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not use more force than in the gentle flesh, as in legs, and arms, and hands, and fingers, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and at no time does one make another instrument small, resembling the scoops of fists, according to this form, for which one staunches blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it nowhere near the place that joins the veins, and the arteries, and nowhere near according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	At no time do they swell the hands of any men when their corruption begins, as much as they seem like women's hands;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain lame and swollen, and who want to cure them, thus it is necessary to soothe according to this form of this line, up to G.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scoop out the fat, and apply the medicinal plaster to the raw flesh, then bring together the two lips of the wound to suture, and cure until it is healthy;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and you press the slender limb down, and it is relaxed by its greatness just like they do with women, if they are in the second rib, through similar fissures;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	because one is held by the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line B to the line G;
