puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and prepare what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, so that it be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healthy, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the corruption of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive oil;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it heal as much as it absorbs the residue and fat, then cure it so it becomes healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the seats
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from beneath the seats are kinds of hard scrofulous tumors which have ribs, and there is only moisture that they contain.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who hold moisture must be treated according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply an ointment to bring healing to those who are wounded.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, do it as we have said in cases of scrofula, and if the wound becomes swollen, apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is broken, and the skin is swollen which is above, then many abscesses come from it, and also it happens that the inflamed vein becomes an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one feels it thus, as it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel the strangulation.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is due to the vein, then it appears as a defective rupture.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to touch this abscess, and likewise when it is under the arms and angles and in the collar bone and many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary then to avoid the iron treatment, and he who is in charge should also avoid it, and for he who has inflammation of the artery, make a incision above the skin from afar.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then operate on the waist with onions, and beautifully separate the artery from the membranes, so that it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle beneath it, and make it pierce up to the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread in two eyes, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then puncture the place that is between the two ligaments of an intermuscular area until the blood flows out which is there, and be freed from the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then bring together the treatment that injures not, so that the ligament heals;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal what is wounded, approaching it, so that it may be healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is on the waist of the vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then insert the needle beneath the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and have a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then burst the abscess, as I have told you, or bind one of the two parts as the head of the vein.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread does not come out, then insert another needle under all the threads beneath the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads steady in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut into the abscess until the superfluid comes out, then cut away the superfluid from the heart and let what is tied loose.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a warm dressing with wine and oil, then apply gentle treatments of tents and bandages until he is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the nostrils
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, how abscesses come into the artery and vein, they come into the nostrils when they are inflamed, or from too much hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in joints and toes where there are articulations, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of the body, and it is in many painful conditions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one holds it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not at all in its proper alignment, but beneath the heart.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it must be adjusted from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, neither above nor below, and the one that is in joints cannot be held by iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance it will contract;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those that are on the head or forehead, make the skin on the spatula-shaped.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscesses are small, hold them with a grasp, and cut into their root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, hold it with a clamp, and scrape, then bone and assemble the wound to the sutures, and treat until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	It never happens in the belly and not another similar part, and it is a disease which is called "fungus" by the resemblance of them, and it has subtle roots, and large lumps.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are small and very large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw some that had II or belly wounds that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and were already split, and immediately corroded from moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found one to be 18 ounces heavy, and the other 6 ounces, and the work in the incision is such that you examine if the patient's moisture is moist, and the color of the joint is pale and moist and with subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if you touch the spatula to the large one, and thus are in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For when cutting, there often come too great flows of blood, and if the senses fail you, then hasten to give a hot cautery.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient is frightened and afraid of the incision with iron, take the well-made thread of a thorn, and place the artery as we have said, and let it be for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then hold back, and do not stop constricting the thread of a thorn until it touches the artery, and ease through it without struggle;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, you should be afraid to cut them in the middle of the belly, but you can easily cut most of it, then cauterize so they do not regrow;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then heal the wound, and beware that you do not cut the tendon which is of a fixed color and of poor sensation and of lazy regard;
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of encrusted chancre hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is ripe
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cautery of a wound or incision of the skin, and it is on the belly and in some of the bowls, as it happens in other wounds, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or of windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and it is by the routing of the skin's surface and by the issuing of the bowel, if it is the color of the abscess similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open to diverse issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses with their fingers if it resonates, and then returns, and sometimes it is constricted, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press on it with your hand, it does not constrain at all.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the operations are such that you examine whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in this chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his belly, and be stretched out straight, then sign from below around the navel.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then command to place it between your hands, then go into the limb that you have signed to the entire spatula, then examine the majority of the abscess above the entire great groin.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie it with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let us give the joint a solid hold.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then open the majority of the abscess extended over the joint, and you push your index finger, and seek the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find the true joint, if it dislocates, and pushes the intestine to the defect of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the bowel, if it takes to the groin, and covers the superfluity.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery does you harm contrary, or the vein, if it goes badly in, then return to your work and take two needles, and push two strong threads, and push the two needles into what you have done in a cross that you make pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in three places under the skin, and if you see it, remove the skin, and let the pus drain out until it disperses, and separate the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	where you cut when it is subtle and porous, then treat what needs to be treated, and shave the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the limb of what needs to be treated, and sew the limb.
dou chancre	because of an ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken in the division about the similarities of cancer, and how one should operate with medicines, and how one should avoid the treatment with iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say that cancer grows in the marrow, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when cancer is in the limb or where it can be rooted like a cancer that is in the breasts, and in the hips, and in similar places, and one must remove everything when it is at the beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is old and chronic, you must not approach it, for I know of no one who can heal it.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	I never saw anyone heal it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the treatments, when it is in its place or where you can open it, as we have said, is that you should purge the patient of black bile several times;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him healthier if he has shown repletion, then prepare the patient for a good place to perform the treatment;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then cut your ulcers or tumors, and shave all parts, and remove all decay without leaving anything.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and press well with your hand or anything, and if the blood spurts out against the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize until the bleeding stops.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of another treatment as long as he is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment that is done with medicines, and that which is cured by iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is suddenly inflamed;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not touch with iron in these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	it is to know, tympanitis and hypochondria, for it is mortal things;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	then when you medicate this similarity of dropsy which is called "inflamed" by medicines, and the treatment does not profit, if you see that the patient is weak, or if they have another disease besides dropsy, such as a tumor and solution of stomach and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if you do not touch with iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient is very virtuous, and he has no other disease than dropsy only, and it is not too young nor too old, then so should you operate:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	raise the patient's right hand on your hands, and the assistants press the belly in bulging out the water at the lowest part of the thigh, then take the spine of the back according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	to a point, and in no way should it not be so entered that it can come just up to the intestine when one fixes it in, and it cannot be blocked;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look if the dropsy is inclined towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you make an incision thus of the belly, you must straighten up above the navel;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is due to the disease of the liver, then make your incision on the left side of the belly;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to weakness, let it be on the right side, and it is not suitable that the patient leans on the crack that the surplus flows do not run to the weak spot;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and cut, and lift your hand to the entire spatula between the skin and the siphac as if scraping out the quantity of an ounce or so much therein;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the siphac as much as the spatula reaches the empty spot, and it is the level of the water, then pull it back, and you will cut with this instrument in the shape that is there;
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a subtle silver tube, and it is of a lightweight material or alloy, and has a small hole at the lower part;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and where it is narrowed on one side, it has three holes;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and one from another part, and one from another;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut like a pen, and it's the shape of the incision where the writers cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top is the scalpel, so that when the instruments come to the water, they descend now onto the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty the quarter or third part, for if you empty more than it is necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient may die from the loss of his spirit's arm, or he falls into a swoon, or approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then draw the instrument and hold the water, and it is held back now by the cord which stops up the passage that is on the syphac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then recommend the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and remove a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do it no day, and keep from flowing as long as it does not remain but a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much water, if the treatment of the tomb or gravel heats up, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and you should refrain from drinking.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the treatment with drying medicines so that it be healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the stopping of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	There never grows a child who has no hairs on the penis, or the hairs are small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If you want to pierce as soon as possible without making a large wound, make a very subtle incision according to this form.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or thrust I into the subtle closure of the bladder, and tie it thus for three days or four, and when it wants to make urine, so be it opened, and let it urinate, and then put it back.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance they do not cover it, for the urine that comes out does not allow them to keep it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Here is the translation:
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the passage in their back are afflicted, for none are born with the passage at the head of the penis, because they cannot urinate until they lift their penis high.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come to the marrow, and it's a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is that the patients lie thus on their back, then they stretch out the head of the penis and the skin as well as the length of a pen, so that the passage takes in the middle, just as it should.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the flow of blood that comes many times, and if it happens, then staunch what is bleeding blood, and heal the wound until it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times they come to this bath, and it is a show of bad flesh.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malignant and non-malignant ones;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	you must take them to the subtle onion, and cut and bind all of them, then put on cotton wool in Egyptian ointment;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with diafinicon ointment until it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and putrid, then you must apply fire cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it, and the bath is in a similar state to the edge, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the bath that is inside first;
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is cleansed, then heal what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you cure them together, it is not assured that the flesh of the edge will not be perceived, and blackness and corruption come into his edge and in his groin;
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood comes, then one must apply the lunar cautery according to this method:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery helps with these two combined dispositions:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	it is to know, at the decay of blood, and at the corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the stick is corrupted and withdrawn, it is necessary that you apply or conduct a vein's channel of lead, and urinate the patient amidst;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin is dry at the head of the stick which has to do with those who have not been circumcised, or it has to do with a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with a sharp instrument, so much that the ligaments are disentangled, and the head of the stick is freed from all parts;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a grievous thing to devise this, then it is necessary that you scrape it with a spatula or some pointed instrument at the head of the stick and of the skin;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then remove the bandage gently between two, and I place the subtle layer of the millstone in cold water, so that it does not dry up again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Surgery is not a matter of continuing as with other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	In every way when we do this work of our will, and properly with children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not circumcise their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of my masters and healthy men who performed circumcision around the thigh, with force, and at every new occasion;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if the course was altered because there were two tunics, and by chance it happened that one was cut above and the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Now the wound is covered, and the pain is double, and at the mundification which is in the thigh, it is not assured of the point of the limb;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and at the Mundification of the ankle by chance it happens that the vein is pierced, and they run the abscess, and many times they are born thus that they have no need of mundification and I wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification which is done with forces at all the thread of the wire I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut equally in all souls tension;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread should be well stretched around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not make him suffer more than to tie the thread around the penis so gently, and then you make it slide in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then you make it stand straight between your hands, and hold the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then put your hand on the penis and blow or make a sign, and pull it up high so that the head of the penis is inside;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then well-cleanse the ordure that is assembled there, then tie the sign with a double thread, then tie it underneath I push to another lien.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it as you ought to by the second ligature at the pouch and at the index finger, and copulate between the two ligatures, then lift the cord above hastily and pull the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the remedy.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and on the powder I drizzle glue from a moth-eaten egg cooked at the same time as rose water, mixed with rose oil good and fresh, and let it stay until the next day, and treat with another treatment as long as he is not healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the remedies for the purification is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two heads should be opposite and should be cutting, and should be the heads also as big as the equal measurement:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of mundification is when the heart within was opened at the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then it is necessary that you stretch it to your finger, thus that the liquids make an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and the equal alignment, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, so hold it with bandages, and then the cope.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if it surpasses three days, and that which is beneath the rod is inflamed, so let it be until the abscessed place is appeased, and the crust scales lightly;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you cover it as you can move, and guard against the part of the rod, this will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Heal then the wound of things suddenly wounded by powder, which we have said to treat with powders, and if you cover it beyond measure, and it goes to the surface, it will not harm at all.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure the wounds, as we have said, until they are healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from obstruction of the stone, or congealed blood, or bubble, or new flesh, or similar things, which we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine does not flow, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is there or in the neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient be bent over their knees;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and they place their feet on the back, and stretch out their belly from the upper part of the back, and restrain the patient's arm as much as he can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constricted at the expression of the stone above, because of which the urine flows;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you administer an extraction with all the instrument called "syringe", of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and be of subtle silver threads, like the feather of a bird;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let it be the length of a palm and a half, and be subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the method of releasing the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it at the head with a piece of wool or cotton, and push the head of the thread into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut the excess of the wool and push it just to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and wolf's cub's urine, and make the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and the rod of moist oil and olive oil and water TED;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the rod, until it reaches the root of the rod, then bend the rod downwards towards the bowel;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then apply the syringe before reaching the bladder, and the patient feels it going up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order because of that which conducts or guides it when it twists.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then stretch the thread throughout the little lane little by little, and the urine follows the lane, then it is straightened out, and makes the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And continue with the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the vein
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or blood comes into the vein, where putridity is assembled, and you have seen distilled waters and medicines, if made on all the instrument called "clyster", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if there are three perforations:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see.
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the veins are sought by which the short medicine is such that it stops well the sensual movement without addition, if one can then draw out the moisture, and apply as needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see your medications in the bladder, place the head of the cauterizing iron in the moisture, and pull towards the drawing force that is within.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you draw the moisture to the cauterizing iron, and then strongly pull back the drawing force within.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture enters there, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and it is the subtle form of the syringe through which one injects the bladder.
si est ci:	if it is so.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or of copper, and it has a head that is higher.
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below is the seat or the chain's end.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in it that you want to inject into the bladder, then tie it between the two seats in the form of a double twisted thread, and heat that moisture over the fire.
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then put the head of the cauterizing iron on the rod, then hold your hand on the bladder with all the moisture collected there, until the patient feels that the moisture has been drawn into the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle with it, and pierce it roundly all around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a buckle, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as if you had done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already said in the previous section the ways of piercing and the extraction of assembled medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and we have said the difference between the piercing for painful wounds, and all the signs, and in which piercing one should operate with skill;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the rod;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	And I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is generated in the bladder happens more often to children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it appears suddenly, and scratches the patient's rod, and it bites many times, and then becomes swollen;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and at most of these jumps the foundations;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is easy to heal children until they are 4 years old, and it is very grievous in the old, and it is like a weak moan, to those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and it is easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to clean the patient through cleansing, in order to remove all the bad humors that are within the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders the healing of the wound.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift them up and move them downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and jumps out many times from the top high;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then have him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the vessel is entirely sloping downward.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then the scalpel and touch within;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall to the toucher of the whole, then anoint your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is weak, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and accomplished;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and thrust it into its foundation, and cut into the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, then anoint the neck of the vessel;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on with your finger, and thrust into the defect where you saw to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the minister to press the vessel with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand above the loins, and with his left hand lift the skin which is beneath the loins in the part where the cutting is done.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then I apply the spatula-shaped instrument, because this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make an incision between that which is between the groin and the perineum, not in the middle but on the left side of the navel;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be straight on the stone, and the two should be thus or at the perineum, and the cut should traverse so that it is wide enough by default, and within it is narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	perhaps the pressure if the two which are at the perineum, so that it may sense the labor;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is a piece of stone where it has angles and margins:
si est griés a issir;	if it is difficult to come out;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is a piece that is underneath, similar to a pebble, and rounded, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Where there are angles and margins, make the cutting larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and it does not jump, so it is necessary that you stretch on the tendons which are like a thread at the head, in order to stretch the stone so it does not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	where you apply beneath the subtle, curved instrument at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot engineer it thus, so enlarge the small hole, and if the sense is deceived, so extract the glassy [substance];
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one stone, so apply the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then extract forcefully, and the small ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be treated with caution, and made to cause less harm.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For these things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	where he dies, or the urine comes back through the tube that the veins cannot hold;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but however you exert yourself to treat, or to remove the bandages, so that you treat it by sections;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, then apply the plaster of incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it in place, and put on top a dressing moistened with oil and wine, or with oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then restore the patient to their bed, and do not dislodge the bandage until just a day later.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, stir well the oil and water, then apply the ointment of diafinicon and ointment of basilicon, until he is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot abscesses come in the wound and corrode, and there is congealment of blood in the bladder, and so it retains the urine, which is known in such a way that without a sound with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	put your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrode the bladder, and putrefy;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound of water and of oil and of wax, and aid it in all ways that you know, so that it may be healthy.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the openings that you treat, that you tie the two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is conducted by the rod, and fixed in, and the urine cannot issue;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the treatment of what I say thus, that you cut often, is to excuse oneself from cutting by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already experienced this thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Here is the translation:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take the thread and tie it around the rod beneath the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then push the iron into the rod gently, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the iron with your hand in the stone little by little, until you can break the stone from another side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If you come so soon to the urine, then press your hand on what is remaining of the stone that is within the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	It is thus broken, and jumps out with the urine, and heals the patient;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this because of any thing that deflects it, then put the thread beneath the stone and another above, then make the penis in place of the stone between the two ligaments, then extract it out, and release the ligament, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until he is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It rarely happens that a stone is in the genitals of women, and if it happens at all, the treatment is grievous, and is defended against by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well who uncovers herself as mirrors, especially when she is cast.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman who knows well in this art of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more profound than the stone of the man, because it requires making a deeper cut, and great fear there is. And if you need to ascend to this, then it is necessary that you take a wise woman knowing well, and touch the true vein on, and if you do not find it, nevertheless seek I cast a subtle mirror;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and it presents a wise woman in the life of women, where a woman who knows part of the art, and commands that she does what you command her to do from the inquiry of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look well if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to push his finger or foundation and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if he finds it, if it presses beneath his finger, and he recommends that she pushes her finger or with the patient, and seeks and presses his left hand on the bladder strongly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it gently from the entrance of the bladder down to beneath, until it comes to the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then feel upon the stone at the root of the thigh against the soft flesh, there where it is most apparent, and feel the stone in that part;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his finger upon the stone or beneath, and let it be cut at the first small size;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then put the razor in the incision, if you feel the stone if it grows into the wound as much as the stone can issue forth, and know that many kinds of stones are:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	it is to know, small and large and thick and thin, long and round, and those that have roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to recognize the issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the saneness (health) fails, then apply to the liver a vitroil broth, and hold for an hour as long as the saneness is established;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is broken, and use the instruments that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone as men do for you to help in your operation;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the saneness (health) fails, and it is of the artery that is cut, then apply the powder to the liver and hold with tentes and bendelz, and do not recommence more than this, and leave the stone and do not handle it again, lest by chance the patient may die;
puis cure la plaie.	then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the spots are purified, then return to your work, so that the stone can come out forcibly.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Armice water is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white foam, which is beneath the skin of the loins, that contains the egg.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac", and never is properly on the fabric of the eyelid, if one thinks that it is another eyelid;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it's the skin of the conjunctiva between the white "syfac" that we have mentioned;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and they do not have a small pouch.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from the weakness that comes to the intestines, and it spreads out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never does it come from percussion on the conjunctiva, and this moisture if it has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	where it is declining in color to yellowish, or it is without red, or black, or whitish blue, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is or white "syfac" that we have mentioned, then it is the red abscesses, a little long as the figure of an eye, and does not open the conjunctiva, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in its own fabric, then are the abscesses formed with part of the vein, and for this reason one thinks that it is another vein.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white sifac, then it feels very good;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you want to know the color of the moisture, it is tested at all the internal quartering, from which the form is thus presented.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the examination, judge from what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure by iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his power and the replenishment of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then he leans on his back, on something a little high, and places beneath him many towels;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then he sits on his left, and instructs the minister to sit on the right, and stretches out the rod to one of the two ribs of the heart of the joints;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the scalpel lightly, and cut the skin of the joints within the length of a hand up to the point where it pricks, and let your incision be entirely straight in dividing the skin of the joints up to the white spot, and carefully scrape off subtly as you can.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the white spot fully with a large perforator, and extract all the water, and then put in your anointed fingers, and the white spot is above.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	And do not touch the core of the joints, but only the white spot should be scraped.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cut all or in pieces the membrane of it subtly, so that if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	And if the egg-shaped fluid flows out for a long time, then you will reset it in its place when you have accomplished the work of the white spot.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then assemble the two leaves of skin around the burn with a suture, then treat it like other wounds until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the ulcer corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you lift the veins that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cut around the entire suspension, and extract the ulcer, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the water is gathered in two assembled parts, know that these are two branches.
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	Cut the other part similarly as you did the first equally, then suck out the blood, and put into the wounded place a moistened oil rosate.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another moistened linen in wine and oil, and put on the two burns, and put doubled drapels above, and tie it with all the bandages that are according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take II drapels, and the applications of laine charpie according to this resemblance and are assembled by stitching in the girdle of the arms, and one of the heads takes hold on the foundation just up to the back, and the others at the part where they prick.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two heads on the II angles, and so is all assembled the restraint in the buckle of the arm;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and no time is medicine this remedy of cautery in the length of iron, and it is that you take I cautery cultellary subtle, and burn the skin of the thighs, and be scorched as we have said, so that the white vein that contains the water is discovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that vein as onions, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery;
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And hold the scalp in all the ways you can, as much as you stretch it.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and beware that the flames do not touch the egg;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more sacred;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and beware of the deterioration of blood, and beware that the operations are timely;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing makes you do the opposite, or abscess bursts or deterioration of blood or something else, if you cure what makes you do the opposite, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to undergo this operation due to its horror, if you promise perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs we have said that the aqueous humour is there, then make the patient sit on a high seat;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess in the part beneath all the spatula-like width, and put the perforation deep into the long body of the corpse;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the wounds be large, so that all the pus flows out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let it flow out to discharge the remaining pus, then treat it until the wound is healthy;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not allow the pus to exit through the mouth of the wound, it is necessary that you insert a tube or instrument through which one extracts the pus of hydropic people, so that its shape is thus presented;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound, and know that the pus returns, and it is assembled after six months or a year, and when it is assembled as before, then the patient will spend their days thus.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the entrails
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the treatment of this disease there is fear in many dispositions, because it seems to me that many are worth more than those left behind.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you about the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come from corruption, and likewise from bad humors;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is in most cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to be known by the abundance of bitter and acidic humor, which is spread through bad humors, or from percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and there is no point of pain, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance it is a grievous abscess, greenish and piercing, and of a foul color, and sometimes it comes from a narrowing of the artery, or from an inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a narrowing of the artery, it is recognized by the disposition of the hot abscess, when you press on it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and do not touch him with your hand.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	He who is made of inflamed vein is known by his expression at the touch of the fingers, and one can well judge the condition from this resemblance, and on other flesh.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the cord of the veins, then the vein is above, and the flow falls from the white surface, and releases the suspension from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the vein is already familiar with these new flesh, then it is necessary that you extract the vein, and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is attached to the surface, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is necessary that you release all of this tension, and cut around it circularly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is at the back of the hand, then it is necessary to cauterize all of it, and hold the finger steady, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the operations are accomplished, then apply the plaster of softening oil and rose oil, and afterwards treat with other treatments until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the entrails
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	These are enclosed abscesses wrapped in a wrapping resembling a bundle, with the softening of the veins, and the patient suffers greatly when it bursts.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this disease is very similar to the previous one, and in every way we will tell you about its work, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you seat the patient on a high seat, then bind him with suspensory cords at the two hips, to all the vessels which are close to the vertebrae, and tighten them firmly, and stretch them out strongly;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut with a sharp spatula widely through the spot where the vessels are, until they are discovered, and then scrape away from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then fix a needle where it has a double thread, and tie it to the first vein where the vitellus is come, and then tie it again to the other vein;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then they apply the cupping glass directly, according to the length of the body, and in drawing out the corrupted humors;
