puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then heal the wound as with others or by applying a poultice, so that no vessel bursts which would nourish one of the intestines;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for through this there comes no harm, and if all the vessels come together, it is necessary to extract the intestines from all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and dry out, and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	about the treatment of swelling
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The symptoms of this disorder are through the section that comes or goes out, or the extension onto the belly in the area of the intestines, because the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the intestines;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is either from the softness of the intestine, or from the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	from percussion, or from a fall, or from a blow, or from lifting of a heavy weight, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is about the extension of the muscle, if it happens little by little, in a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and they are equal abscesses right up to the peritoneum, because the muscle presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the swelling of the intestine, which causes sudden severe pain at the beginning, and there are diverse abscesses appearing beneath the skin nearby, and this is due to the issue with the intestine and the body's weakness against the swelling of the intestine.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it descends with the intestines, and is retained inside, and causes great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments of fear, because they think they will escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the surgery is that you instruct the patient to insert their intestine with their hand inside the wound, if they can reinsert it.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then let him be supported on his neck between your hands, and lift the hips;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch out the heart upwards, and cover all the skin of the thighs from the length.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put inside the liver of the waist uncines according to what you need to open the wound, and be such that the eyes can issue forth.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scrape the dead skin which is under the skin of the joints, so that the white skin underneath becomes uncovered on all sides;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	Then put your finger index in the one that follows the joint, in the one that is between the white skin which is under the skin of the vein, and between the second skin, and separate what is behind the vein, and between the second skin;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move the vein to the right hand within the circle of the joints, and stretch the white skin upwards with your left hand, and lift the vein against all the skin towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the assistant to stretch the vein upwards, and separate what is behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and seek with your fingers if there is a point of the intestine enveloped or hard white skin, and if you do not find anything, put it to the belly below;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	Then take a needle with a large thread made of X threads, and insert it into the rear part of the skin, which is after the skin of the kidneys.
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the waist, then cut the heads that appear as threads, so that there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the skin with a strong thread of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the heads of the threads, and tie them firmly in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, lest an abscess forms there;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put the thread there again according to the first thread, as long as two fingers from that one, and after these two threads leave the skin which is under the skin of the kidneys the width of a finger;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part which is beneath the skin of the thighs, as far as the sinew and the bowel, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then mix the millstone in oil, and put it on wounds, and I will mix the lien that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at no time is the white finger cauterized which we have said, after the incision, due to fear of deterioration of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens often, and let the lien stay until it dries by itself;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it delays in drying, so be aroused with warm water, and put on what we have said, until it dries;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then heal the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healthy.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I never saw anyone who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones said that it is done as with the twig that grows together with the vein, in such a way that you bind the vessels, after cutting lightly underneath.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	Then cauterize in the middle, and treat the abscess of those who are swollen, so that the veins heal.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, so that it becomes healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	No time is spent on rough remedies, as we have said, and open the abscesses.
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not descend into the intestines with caustics, and if they descend, it is little, and repair all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and always, if it stays too long in this point, the wound or syrup believes, so that the intestines descend;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the syrup which is in the abscesses, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and inflates the abscesses and opens.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the treatment is by cauterization, as we have previously said.
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and it is never cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and it is that the patient places himself on his back between your hands, then take the limb of the affected joint in a straight line according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the skin that is beneath the skin which is swollen, then take the razor and place it on the apparent limb beneath the skin;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press at the front of the belly, then cut the two apparent limbs beneath the skin on the head of the razor, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the razor, and do not touch the skin in any way that would stretch one finger to another, as I have made you aware of in the treatment of the rupture of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then heal by the healing of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the fibers, if it is disfigured and cures the wound, so that it may be healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The surface is constricted, and has no appearance in the wound, and the cauteries are muted in this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the thighs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times are softened the skins of the joints in some men, because the flesh that is within is softened, and it is easy to see;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure, that one makes the patient sit up straight and covers the skin which is softened on the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring together the two lips of a wound, and if you see, first remove the excess of softened skin at three stitches or four firmly;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cover between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healthy, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	of punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that cauteries are condemned in our law, and therefore I please that I do not speak of them in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is not necessary to use them for two reasons:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the masters know how to respond when one asks them, and about the cure;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have need of cautery on certain beasts to aid us, such as goat and sheep and cattle and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say then that cauteries are made according to two manners:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	or by attraction, or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In that which we make by attraction, let us sit in warm water, as long as the joint becomes softened and relaxed;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then take them with your hand, until they are reset and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the cautery of incision:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you hold the best, and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then tie the suspensor, and cover each hole with a cup, when you have well scarified them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and let no pus accumulate under the skin and the subtle skin that is above the veins;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of cautery is more deadly than that which is made by attraction, because in attraction sometimes something of the joints remains, which prevents the joint from being luxated;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then heal the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	Here is the translation:
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways in men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	One is when between the two testicles appears as if it were the figure of a woman's nature, where it has hair, and sometimes the urine flows in a short distance.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is in women, and it has on the little finger as a rod and they bind.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of the man and woman is that you treat the adjacent flesh entirely, and you heal as for other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second way, of men whose urine passes through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tentiginous (Note: Tentiginous likely means "inflamed" or "swollen", but I'll keep it as close to the original as possible)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	A tumor is an adjacent flesh on the natural part, so much that it is too ugly to behold;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you remove the excess of the tumor with your hand or with onions, and treat it lightly.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not go too deeply into the fontanelle, because the running of blood will not come, then the treatment of another treatment until it is healthy;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and at another time it rises to the mouth of the marrow, and the impediment, and by chance it bursts forth, and is according to the resemblance of a cowe, and for this they called it in ancient times "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary to cauterize it, just as we have said for the tetanus, and to treat it until it is healthy.
de erratique	of the erratic (Note: Erratique likely means "irregular" or "wayward", but I'll keep it as close to the original as possible)
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Error occurs when the nature of the woman is not fully perceived, or the passage is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and it is natural from birth, or happens by accident through disease that comes to it;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is from a stuck cartilage, or subtle and thick dou syfac, and it is made in the fontanelle of the marrow, or in the ribs, or below, or whatever;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and difficulty conceiving, and infertility, and by chance having flowers to have;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this thing is by the observation of the pill.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears close, seek it in your fingers or in the vein.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is a subtle and dou syfac, and it is near the two lobes, if you hurry, and turn them thus:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	put your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then extend the two lobes formally, so that the subtle dou syfac is round, and is above the protuberances;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take a linen cloth, and anoint it with oil, and place it on the loins, and guide the woman to her husband every day, so that she cannot become pregnant.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the wound is hard and thick, it is necessary to wash the scalpel with a similar leaf of mint.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the protuberances are of flesh born, then suspend them from the ninth rib and the cope;
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and these bloody medicines are stagnating blood, if as an antidote, blood of dragon, incense, together with abundant dew;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	Then apply a wide poultice of soft cloth, so that the wound cannot suppurate;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and let it be for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be cured by other treatments until he is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh wounds become gangrenous, then they need to be covered according to this manner, so that they do not turn into abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is gangrenous in the flesh, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are varices of veins that without sharp custom, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thrombosed;
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will tell you here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the veins, when they are deeply embedded in the flesh, and they do not appear to sensation, if it is not the cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the flesh, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then stop the flow as with tourniquets, and bind around its roots, then powder with medicines that restrain blood, such as açaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then soak her feet in warm water for an hour, then put them in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if blood flows out, then make him sit in a decoction of sumac and crust of pomegranate seeds and of gale and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster on his back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stagnates, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If that does not work, make him apply warm poultices to the back and to the affected limbs without piercing;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	then take wool, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of angelica with old wine, and apply warm to the location.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess breaks, then clean the location of the swelling as much as it is healthy;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a rough head, then it should be covered as I have said before;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then heal him so that he may be healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come in the marrow, such as cancer and piercing abscesses and herpes and isthmuses and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary therefore that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that collect pus.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, look if the abscesses are gathered at the beginning of their coming, and full of bitterness and fever, and if it becomes red then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make me soften until the pain is appeased;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have small seats or where he leans back, and support himself on his back and gather his feet together in order to deflect the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his hips be expanded, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good ligament;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	Then suck the bulb towards the right side, and I will handle the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the marrow, from which afterwards comes the form.
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you have handled this instrument, you fix the rule first to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and it does not harm the patient.
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instruments are too large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with drapels, so that the instruments do not harm them.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he place the horn of the instrument above, and that he hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscesses open, and one feels them with the hand, it is necessary to cover at the head, with a spatula-like instrument.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the wound is empty, it is necessary that you put in the place tender mosses in oil rose, or in dry green oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and apply the tender flesh to the bottom of the wound, and put beneath the marrow and beneath the prickly vein clean moss in water or soft mallow being applied;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the treatment after two days of anointing comes to that, so that it be healthy;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and often lift up the marrow and the wound with a cluster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and aristology being applied for a long time;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the anointing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is returned to the marrow, it is necessary that you beware of iron rust, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of the swelling
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is necessary to be first at the childbirth that it knows the natural shape of the infant, and the signs are when you see the woman approaching from below, and desires to give birth to the arm;
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then hasten the edges of the iron to issue;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	then consider that these instruments are according to natural figure, and it is the issue under its head, and the second one with it;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, then you should press his belly lightly, so that the edges issue quickly;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when it descends upon its head, then is the second one with it, and the marrow of its superfluities is purified by good mundification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes sometimes upon its feet, and comes against the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or swelling, and is converted by accident over its neck, and by other bad figures;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	it is necessary for the practitioner to be wise and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one must aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the infant comes onto its head by natural means, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the strength of the child is weak, then make it sit on a cushion, or the women hold it;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and raise its natural oil or fenugreek being cooked, and then put the bath between its two small spatula-like fingers where it is formed:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and anoint the umbilical cord, and cut to his nail as much as the moisture that is in there flows out;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press the woman's belly as much as the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clysterize the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and oil of sesame;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make her take and be comforted by condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	if the infant is now astral.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands are swollen, then it is necessary to reset them lightly little by little.
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a seat, and lift her feet high;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then remove the seat from the ground, and hold the woman, so she does not fall at the removal.
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot enter, and the infant is dead, then grasp the hands at the cot which is placed before, and extract the child, and reset equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes onto its feet, it is necessary to push high up;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is equalized;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take hold of the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps just to the hips, then instruct to take hold, and make it stretch with good condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If the wound is deep, then God wants.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not straighten as we have said, if it turns a little and a little, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not heal as we have said, take a poultice of high quality, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and crush everything in the mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put it on the woman's nature within and drive out this ointment, then make her sit in warm water until beneath the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is softened underneath, make her a girdle of myrrh, and put it underneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a seat, then make her stretch out and hold her mouth and nose, and take her belly lightly, for the infant is coming out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes out in this form, then I put the fontanel of its hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then let it be sewn onto its neck, and the feet depend below, and let it be leaning on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold its hands a little at a time, and then place its hands on the belly, and remove the cushions from below, until it is arranged below;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if it does not sit well, take its feet and shape them comfortably, then shape the belly above, then you will place your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and rock the child a little at a time;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to take hold of it until the child is seated.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes holding a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to skillfully bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then lift the woman, and go.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed, and shape her legs comfortably.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the poultice that I have prepared;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if it does not take, let it sit on the seat, then study to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and look at the child according to its natural shape, and let it stretch out, and instruct it to take hold as much as the veins can be forced.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of the child on his neck, and has spread out his hands, and his face turned towards his mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I think that the vein should take its hand, then turn it little by little, and look at it lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, put on the natural poultice of altée and oil, as we have said, then instruct it to move little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, let it sit on the seat, and instruct it to take hold;
et la fai esternuer.	and let it stretch out.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all the following
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be in this manner entirely the second time, cut the second time at your finger, as much as the moisture is evacuated;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and he presses his face against his neck, if the cup of the womb, so it is not retained, and kills the infant;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then throw the child inside, as long as you have placed it so it fits, and instruct the woman that she should not take it out at any time:
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will be easier to deliver.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the dislocation of the twins (likely referring to a joint or a pair of bones)
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and it is not a strange thing, and it happens little.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, if they have little name;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that, for they are multiplied, and are divided by the syphac who separates them, which is tied to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they issue forth naturally as a single one, just like we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if it is grievous, so the treatment as we have said, and let the subtle baths, and make everything easy and light that it does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it will bring health to him.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	None are formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and all are formed in the form of an infant by the measurement of the glorious wisdom, and it is necessary that the baths know everything, for it seems that similar things have happened;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman with a dead or stillborn child, as I have said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to perform manual extraction;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and there is no accident or she has fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be bent over her back, and her hands be inclined downwards, and the legs be raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife holds the two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not torn apart during the delivery of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mother with oils made from leaves of wild tansy and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint her hands with these oils and musk;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then gently lay them in the mother's lap, then she wants the place where she laid the swaddling clothes to be comfortable for her, and take care that the infant is well wrapped so it descends onto its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if you fasten the swaddling clothes in her eyes or on her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or under the beard or in the armpit or near the ribs, and if the descent is onto the feet, hold it or prick it and touch the moistened sides;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary to hold the onion in his right hand, and put the curve between the fingers of his left hand, and hold his whole hand lightly, and fix the onion in none of these places that we have said, until it reaches the desired spot.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and it is the shape of the onion:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then fix an encounter with another onion, or the third where you have your mastery, so that the extractions are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then they are evenly stretched by moving one way and another, to make them issue forth, and let the onions be held firm, as is their shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, anoint the vein with some of its oil, and apply it to that part, and pull out the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains none, put this onion or higher up, and do it until everything issues forth completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be reduced by stretching, then it is necessary that you envelop it with a bandage, so long as it becomes straight.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	Then put a bandage on the joint of the sole or at the ankle, and thus it is necessary that you do the same with the other hand, and so for the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the head of the infant is large and it is twisted in its exit, or if it has an aching assembled head, then it is necessary that you put the spinal instrument between your two, and make the head straight and extract the ach.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you will use the instrument called "almidach", which is made with the instruments or chapter that follows this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus the same make the infants have a naturally straight head.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then treat the bones with tongs, and if the head jumps out and holds on to the malleolus, so be careful, as much as the moisture that is or worse issues;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut into pieces at the joint where you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, then it is necessary that you puncture as much as the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the inflammation is on its feet, then it is light attraction, and the adjustments at the mouth of the morrow are lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stretched in the belly or in the thigh, then it is necessary that you extract it with the drapil enveloped on the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and open the belly or the thigh, as much as the moisture that flows from it;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other members are numbed, and the head remains, then put the scalpel in the palm of your hand at the front of the marrow, and treat it just up to the mouth of the marrow;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	Then apply the ninth or tenth treatment, and burn the excess flesh.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed by hot abscess that has come, if it does not need to be operated on, then it needs to be treated with moist and fatty things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and treat the ulcers, and apply ointments that are mild, softening, and moisturizing.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its side, and you can place it evenly, then treat it as we have said regarding the living infant.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and do not have any power, if you burn the flesh in pieces, and leave nothing of the secondary (layer).
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, treat them as we have said regarding hot abscesses that come into the marrow.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if a flow of blood comes out, then apply astringent ointments, and treat with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly an infant had been dead, then she conceived another on top of that, and the other was stillborn.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came abscesses in his stomach, and they grew so much that they burst open, and he began to have great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not soothe the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed on it a strong plaster, and an bone came out, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel greatly, because this wind has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I examined the wound and treated it with my hands, as much as the woman was at a better point;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I watched the woman for a long time afterwards, and it immediately improved a little bit around the joint;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I did not record this chapter further because, when the masters find a strange thing, they know how to put it right.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the hammer to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Hereafter comes the method of pressing, where one finds the books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and it is given to two attendants as it is given to the heads of the veins.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle on the constrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the tube be of a large size, and the margin of the trees as it should be, and of one palm and a half;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in the two veins let there be adjustments of this same tube, which are closed at one and the other, by half a palm in length or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and this adjustment is pushed into the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, in its more subtle and lighter resemblance, is made from ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of the tenons.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it has two heads two adjustments, as you see, of a palm's length, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you want to open the marrow with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and legs covered, then push the two adjustments adjusted together into the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument down between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then operate your hand on the entire instrument, as you have done with the tenons equally, according to the quantity that you want to open the mouth of the marrow, until the handle does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all superior, and are multiplied for their similar appearances;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the eyes have them aligned, so much more swift is the work, and higher are the homes for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not appeared to, for their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second one is retained in infancy, then you must command the patient to retain his wing, and then make him stretch out with confidence, and hold your hands at the mouth and nostrils;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if he jumps through that, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If he does not, take the pot, and make a poultice or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the morrow, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or some of them, being cooked or boiled in water over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	Then put a cane or tube down into the mouth of the patient, and the other end in the hole, and pull it tight so that the vapors come out from inside the patient.
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make it straighten, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondary humor is hastening.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not heal, instruct the patient to apply their left hand in oil of sesame or in a poultice of altaia, and then put it in a warm place, and seek the secondary remedy.
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when they have found it, take it and stretch it little by little directly, so that the patient does not feel pain at the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but you must move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then draw it out.
si venra et se desaerdra.	if it comes and becomes disordered.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the patient is constricted, we have said the treatment to straighten, and of fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and let it not be of all this that we have said, if you guard against falling into error;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it happens that what is at the mouth of the mare, you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then you anoint it with ointment of four drugs;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if it will putrefy and decay, and will come to a crisis;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but always, when it putrefies thus, there comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	It is necessary then to make fumigations suitable for that:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	none of the ancients have experienced fumigation with fresh watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman at the retention of the flowers and of the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to see something similar to a dog, and put the subtle head in nature, and the wide shoulders over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let there be fumigations on the coals, and the tar until it is consumed, and recommence another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their foundation perceived, thus the subtle ones are stifled.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	it is necessary therefore to handle the one who perceives with his finger, and does not perceive it at all from the spatula's agitation, and beware of touching it with the ligature.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the affected limb a mixture of wine and oil, then the treatment of anointing until it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that he will not recover, then put or insert a tube of lead, and leave it there for a long time, and be careful when the veins want to burst in chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And often these stiflings come from a sudden wound or abscess.
si covient coper celui soudement:	it is necessary to cover that suddenly.
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	let it be cured, as we have said about the treatment of a piercing wound.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula at the bottom
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from beneath the foundation are nodation, and larger than those that come from beneath the foundation in default, or in the space of two parts, if there is one fistula or more.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that swelling is old, it is operated on, and beneath the moisture a white or subtle boil appears, and sometimes these fistulae persist;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known by the fact that there is either indigestion or windiness when the patient makes evacuation, and sometimes by chance it jumps into the verse.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the rod;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and they extend just to the joint of the thigh, and just to the top of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And then one recognizes the persistent fistula at the foundation, and it does not go away.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you apply your index finger to the foundation, and insert a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twisting, you insert a subtle probe of lead, or a horse hair, until you feel the probe or the hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from excessive perspiration or wind, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not penetrate well;
si te haste dou curer.	if you hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is close to the bladder or close to the urinary tract, then the urine jumps, and cannot be soothed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	It is perceived just up to the joint of the thigh, if it is the tendon coming just to the loins;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the discovery of pain within, it is that it is still swollen, and no medicine nor sudden relief by anointing;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except through labor, and the foolish doctors who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In those that are not persistent and not ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patients place themselves in your hands on their back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he raises his legs up to his knees, and has his knees bent towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put a straightening tent, or a splint if there is twistedness, until you know where the tent goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it at the bottom, then you should put your right index finger, and then it seems that the tent has penetrated;
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and be discovered where you feel between your finger the siphac or the flesh, then know that it is pierced;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if you do not work carefully, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One can almost always heal some, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that one makes, if it is that one heats the subtle cauterization according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and burn all around the fistula, until it reaches the bottom.
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that these burnt crusts are raised, which resemble a bird's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat the many soft ulcers with a poultice, until those crusts are removed, then treat with ointment, softening and soothing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, nothing else can be healthy;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and hold it between, and do not pierce just to the finger which is at the bottom, and place between your finger and the holder a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering of the vein.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and burn immediately before the holder, and then apply the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the holder.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and it will be delivered the tent, and fall;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then reject those withered branches that seem a bird's wing, and none of them remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound is swollen, and it forms a crust between the skin and the vein, then cauterize with fire or medicine water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cautery assembles two bone things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	it is to know, the dryness of those assembled branches, and the staunching of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the treatment of muddled tents in mud or in broken choz, until the joints throw forth, and it makes the withered branches dry in the mud;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound of the fingers suddenly grown into hard skin, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not relapse again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the edge of the foundation, and is separated from the body, then you should apply your finger or foundation, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between two is the cloth or the syfac or branches, or it is near to piercing, if there are no other ways than the way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	where you apply cautery as we have said, or you cut just to the flesh, or if you can place and treat it as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep in the wound, lest you cut the tendon that holds the foundation, and bring on the evil discharges by the opposite sensation.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healthy, or you separate that covering and the wound then as it is cut from the foundation, either by tension or by another pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then define that empty space which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study how to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part that is deficient in the foundation;
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And often fistulas occur according to this method:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you apply the tent to the fistula, and it is where the foundation of the lesion touches the skin above, if you take a precise tent according to this form at the head:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you push a twisted thread into it, and push the tent onto all the threads in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is penetrating into the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, so that you apply your finger or foundation:
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and draw the head of the thread, and assemble the two edges together, and hold one to the other, and let it be for a day or two:
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it many times, until the threads grasp those flesh that are between them, and cicatrize;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound until it is sewn and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make a copper setting in the depth, and then the treatment, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spinal spine where the fistula is made is very sharp and pointed, partly and cutting;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand not, because one should not grasp what one should not grasp, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the bruises
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Emorrhoids are according to two manners:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	where they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and suddenly blood bursts out, and there is one or many, and they destroy the foundation and at the base of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are deep down have little moisture, and suddenly burst out with a little citrine water or a little blood, and have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those who have them deep in the foundation, is that you instruct the patient to strain themselves to go to the latrine, until the foundations issue forth, and the threads appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and hold it like a tendril, or you hold it on your fingernail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the uncle cannot hold them due to their moisture, take them with a drapil, or a cushion, or a piece of camlet;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and hold them with your fingers, then burn them, and sprinkle above some hot powders that are in the fire of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	where you cauterize as it is said or chapter of cautery, then heal with other treatments until they are healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot issue, then cleanse the patient with a harsh and bitter cluster of medications to purify what is in the foundation, so that they can issue freely;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patients can take it, and if the thread is outside the foundation, then the treatment is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them with your nail or tongs, and burn them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	It is necessary that you adjust the bandage in this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread, and put it on a needle, and then pull the thread above and make a perforation through the needle from another side, and twist the two ends of the thread beneath the needle, and if it is of equal length.
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and hold the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and withdraw the needle, and do likewise for all the others, and leave it there to correct the excessive flow of blood.
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the dressing a soft cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerote, and put it on the base, and instruct the patient that he should rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it be until they scar, and when they will be fallen, if you treat with ointment and other treatments, until he is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the veins or base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Here is the translation:
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	You should reach the point of a spatula or of your nail above the scab, which does not allow it to become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal them as soon as they are numb so that it suits them;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot be numbed, then recommence the rubbing stronger than before, so that it heals much, and is scarred;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal them as soon as they are healthy.
dou fremit	you apply heat
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formice is a small faulty appearance under the skin, and goes much deeper inside;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the frost, and one feels it just like death from shivering, and it comes all over the body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a thread of a bird's feather, or a strong feather of a vulture, and put that thread on the shivering, so that the circles encircle the shivering entirely around;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all around the thread so that you grasp everything around the shivering, and put it deep inside, and eradicate the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a cane of iron or steel in this form, and be subtle below and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	I do not perceive, for I must hold still, and I must press.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, if you cauterize the fremittance, as it is before or in front of the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Never make a cluster of silver or copper, or of tin foil or mail;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and never make those small and large instruments, according to those for which they are prepared.
